pd.DataFrame(table_data).to_csv(f'{table_name}.csv', index=False)\\n    \\n    return tables\\n```\\n\\n## Execution Timeline (6 hours)\\n\\n```\\nHour 0-1: Data loading and feature computation\\n- Load full_data_out.json\\n- Implement syllable counting with CMUdict (pronouncing library)\\n- Implement word frequency lookup (SUBTLEX-US or NLTK)\\n- Compute all features for 13,129 sentences\\n- Save computed features to features.pkl for reuse\\n\\nHour 1-2: Experiment 1 (Bootstrap test for MSE reduction)\\n- Implement paired bootstrap test\\n- Run 10,000 bootstrap samples for both datasets\\n- Compute p-values and confidence intervals\\n\\nHour 2-3: Experiment 2 (Bootstrap CI for coefficients)\\n- Implement bootstrap coefficient CI\\n- Run 10,000 bootstrap samples for both datasets\\n- Identify significant features\\n\\nHour 3-4: Experiment 3 (Proper CV evaluation)\\n- Implement proper cross-validation\\n- Evaluate all three model variants\\n- Generate test set metrics only\\n\\nHour 4-5: Experiment 4-5 (Effect size + Ablation)\\n- Compute Cohen's d for R\u00b2 improvements\\n- Run ablation studies\\n\\nHour 5-6: Output generation and validation\\n- Generate publication-ready tables\\n- Validate results (check for obvious errors)\\n- Save all results to method_out.json\\n```\",\n  \"fallback_plan\": \"## Fallback Plan\\n\\nIf the primary approach encounters issues, the following fallback strategies are available:\\n\\n### Issue 1: Bootstrap Computation Too Slow (10,000 samples \u00d7 13,129 sentences)\\n\\n**Fallback**: Reduce bootstrap samples to 1,000 and use cross-validated OOB estimate.\\n- Use 5-fold CV with bootstrap sampling within each fold\\n- 1,000 bootstrap samples is still sufficient for stable p-value estimates (Monahan, 2008)\\n- Alternative: Use permutation test (999 permutations) which is faster than bootstrap\\n\\n```python\\ndef permutation_test_mse_reduction(X, y, n_permutations=999):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Faster alternative to bootstrap for significance testing.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Compute observed MSE reduction\\n    mse_reduction_observed = compute_mse_reduction(X, y)\\n    \\n    # Permute labels and recompute\\n    mse_reductions_permuted = []\\n    for p in range(n_permutations):\\n        y_perm = np.random.permutation(y)\\n        mse_red = compute_mse_reduction(X, y_perm)\\n        mse_reductions_permuted.append(mse_red)\\n    \\n    # p-value: proportion of permuted statistics >= observed\\n    p_value = np.mean(np.array(mse_reductions_permuted) >= mse_reduction_observed)\\n    return p_value\\n```\\n\\n### Issue 2: CMUdict Syllable Counting Has High OOV Rate\\n\\n**Fallback**: Use heuristic syllable counting for OOV words.\\n- Primary: CMUdict via `pronouncing` library\\n- Fallback for OOV: Use `syllables` package or simple heuristic (count vowel clusters)\\n- Heuristic: syllables \u2248 number of vowel groups (a, e, i, o, u, y)\\n\\n```python\\ndef syllable_count(word):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Get syllable count with CMUdict primary, heuristic fallback.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    import pronouncing\\n    phones = pronouncing.phones_for_word(word.lower())\\n    if phones:\\n        return pronouncing.syllable_count(phones[0])\\n    else:\\n        # Heuristic fallback\\n        vowels = 'aeiouy'\\n        count = 0\\n        prev_was_vowel = False\\n        for char in word.lower():\\n            is_vowel = char in vowels\\n            if is_vowel and not prev_was_vowel:\\n                count += 1\\n            prev_was_vowel = is_vowel\\n        # Adjust for silent e\\n        if word.endswith('e'):\\n            count -= 1\\n        return max(1, count)\\n```\\n\\n### Issue 3: SUBTLEX-US Data Not Available\\n\\n**Fallback**: Use NLTK Gutenberg word frequencies or Google Books Ngrams.\\n- NLTK: `nltk.corpus.gutenberg` provides word frequency counts\\n- Compute frequency as: log(1 + count_in_corpus) / total_words\\n- Alternative: Download frequency lists from https://www.wordfrequency.info/\\n\\n```python\\nimport nltk\\nfrom nltk.corpus import gutenberg\\nfrom collections import Counter\\n\\n# Build frequency dictionary from NLTK word_freq.get(word.lower(), 0)\\n    return np.log1p(count) / total_words  # Normalized log frequency\\n```\\n\\n### Issue 4: Ridge Regression Coefficients Not Interpretable (Multicollinearity)\\n\\n**Fallback**: Use OLS with variance inflation factor (VIF) check, or use Lasso for feature selection.\\n- High multicollinearity can inflate coefficient standard errors\\n- Check VIF: if VIF > 10, remove problematic features\\n- Alternative: Use Lasso to identify important features, then fit OLS on selected features\\n\\n```python\\nfrom statsmodels.stats.outliers_influence import variance_inflation_factor\\nimport statsmodels.api as sm\\n\\n# Check VIF\\nX_with_const = sm.add_constant(X_scaled)\\nvif = pd.DataFrame()\\nvif['feature'] = X_with_const.columns\\nvif['VIF'] = [variance_inflation_factor(X_with_const.values, i) \\n              for i in range(X_with_const.shape[1])]\\n\\n# Remove features with VIF > 10\\nhigh_vif = vif[vif['VIF'] > 10]['feature'].tolist()\\nX_reduced = X.drop(columns=high_vif)\\n```\\n\\n### Issue 5: Bootstrap CI Too Wide (Including Zero When Expected Significant)\\n\\n**Fallback**: Use BCa (bias-corrected and accelerated) bootstrap CI instead of percentile CI.\\n- BCa accounts for bias and skewness in bootstrap distribution\\n- Implement via `scipy.stats.bootstrap` with `method='BCa'`\\n\\n```python\\nfrom scipy.stats import bootstrap\\n\\n# BCa confidence interval\\nres = bootstrap((X, y), statistic=model_coefficient_statistic, \\n                confidence_level=0.95, method='BCa', n_resamples=10000)\\nci_bca = res.confidence_interval\\n```\\n\\n### Issue 6: Datasets Too Large for Memory (If scaled to larger datasets)\\n\\n**Fallback**: memory-efficient bootstrap\\n- Alternative: Use Dask for out-of-core computation\\n\\n### Issue 7: Insufficient Training Data for Stable CV (If using subset)\\n\\n**Fallback**: Use leave-one-out CV (LOOCV) for small datasets, or use repeated CV.\\n- LOOCV: n folds = n samples (use only if n < 1,000)\\n- Repeated CV: Run 5-fold CV 10 times with different random seeds, aggregate results\\n- Recommended: 10 repetitions of 5-fold CV (50 total evaluations)\\n\\n```python\\ndef repeated_cross_validation(X, y, model, n_splits=5, n_repeats=10):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Run repeated CV and aggregate results.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    all_r2 = []\\n    all_mse = []\\n    for r in range(n_repeats):\\n        kf = KFold(n_splits=n_splits, shuffle=True, random_state=r)\\n        for train_idx, test_idx in kf.split(X):\\n            # Fit and evaluate...\\n            all_r2.append(r2_score(y_test, y_pred))\\n    \\n    return {\\n        'test_r2_mean': np.mean(all_r2),\\n        'test_r2_sd': np.std(all_r2),\\n        'test_r2_95ci': np.percentile(all_r2, [2.5, 97.5])\\n    }\\n```\",\n  \"testing_plan\": \"## Testing Plan\\n\\nThe testing plan follows the 'gradual scaling' pattern: start The evaluation addresses five key statistical requirements: (1) paired bootstrap test for MSE reduction significance, (2) bootstrap CI for feature coefficients, (3) proper train/test reporting, (4) effect size analysis, and (5) ablation studies.\\n\\n## Data Loading and Feature Computation\\n\\n```python\\nimport json\\nimport numpy as np\\nimport pandas as pd\\nfrom sklearn.model_selection import cross_val_predict, KFold\\nfrom sklearn.linear_model import Ridge, LinearRegression\\nfrom sklearn.metrics import mean_squared_error, r2_score\\nfrom sklearn.preprocessing import StandardScaler\\nimport scipy.stats as stats\\n\\n# Load datasets\\nwith open('full_data_out.json', 'r') as f:\\n    data = json.load(f)\\n\\n# Extract sentences and readability scores\\n# Dataset format: {\\\"datasets\\\": [{\\\"dataset\\\": \\\"WeeBIT\\\", \\\"examples\\\": [...]}, ...]}\\n\\ndef extract_features(sentences):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute both average and uniformity (CV) features for each sentence.\\n    \\n    Features computed:\\n    - avg_word_length: Mean word length in characters\\n    - avg_syllables: Mean syllable count per word (using CMUdict)\\n    - avg_frequency: Mean word frequency (using SUBTLEX-US or NLTK fallback)\\n    - cv_word_length: Coefficient of variation of word lengths\\n    - cv_syllables: Coefficient of variation of syllable counts\\n    - cv_frequency: Coefficient of variation of word frequencies\\n    - avg_sentence_length: Mean words per sentence (for single sentence, just word count)\\n    \\n    Returns: DataFrame with features for each sentence\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    features_list = []\\n    for sent in sentences:\\n        words = sent.split()\\n        # Word lengths\\n        word_lengths = [len(w) for w in words]\\n        avg_wl = np.mean(word_lengths)\\n        cv_wl = np.std(word_lengths) / (avg_wl + 1e-10)  # Add small epsilon to avoid division by zero\\n        \\n        # Syllable counts (use pronouncing library with CMUdict)\\n        syll_counts = [syllable_count(w) for w in words]  # Implement with CMUdict\\n        avg_syll = np.mean(syll_counts)\\n        cv_syll = np.std(syll_counts) / (avg_syll + 1e-10)\\n        \\n        # Word frequencies (use SUBTLEX-US via NLTK or downloaded file)\\n        freqs = [get_word_frequency(w) for w in words]\\n        avg_freq = np.mean(freqs)\\n        cv_freq = np.std(freqs) / (avg_freq + 1e-10)\\n        \\n        features_list.append({\\n            'avg_word_length': avg_wl,\\n            'avg_syllables': avg_syll,\\n            'avg_frequency': avg_freq,\\n            'cv_word_length': cv_wl,\\n            'cv_syllables': cv_syll,\\n            'cv_frequency': cv_freq,\\n            'sentence_length': len(words)\\n        })\\n    \\n    return pd.DataFrame(features_list)\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 1: Paired Bootstrap Test for MSE Reduction Significance\\n\\n```python\\ndef paired_bootstrap_test(X, y, n_bootstrap=10000):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Test whether adding uniformity features significantly reduces MSE.\\n    \\n    Approach: Paired bootstrap comparing two nested models:\\n    - Model A: Traditional average features only\\n    - Model B: Average + uniformity features\\n    \\n    For each bootstrap sample:\\n    1. Sample indices with replacement (same size as original)\\n    2. Fit both models on bootstrap sample\\n    3. Compute MSE on out-of-bag (OOB) samples\\n    4. Record MSE difference (MSE_A - MSE_B)\\n    \\n    p-value: Proportion of bootstrap samples where MSE_B >= MSE_A\\n    (one-sided test for reduction)\\n    \\n    Returns: p-value, confidence interval for MSE difference\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    n = len(y)\\n    mse_differences = []\\n    \\n    # Feature groupings\\n    avg_features = ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length']\\n    uniformity_features = ['cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency']\\n    \\n    X_avg = X[avg_features]\\n    X_combined = X[avg_features + uniformity_features]\\n    \\n    for b in range(n_bootstrap):\\n        # Bootstrap sample\\n        boot_indices = np.random.choice(n, size=n, replace=True)\\n        oob_indices = np.setdiff1d(np.arange(n), boot_indices)\\n        \\n        if len(oob_indices) == 0:\\n            continue  # Skip if no OOB samples\\n        \\n        # Scale features\\n        scaler_A = StandardScaler()\\n        scaler_B = StandardScaler()\\n        \\n        X_A_boot = scaler_A.fit_transform(X_avg.iloc[boot_indices])\\n        X_A_oob = scaler_A.transform(X_avg.iloc[oob_indices])\\n        \\n        X_B_boot = scaler_B.fit_transform(X_combined.iloc[boot_indices])\\n        X_B_oob = scaler_B.transform(X_combined.iloc[oob_indices])\\n        \\n        y_boot = y[boot_indices]\\n        y_oob = y[oob_indices]\\n        \\n        # Fit models (Ridge for regularization)\\n        model_A = Ridge(alpha=1.0)\\n        model_B = Ridge(alpha=1.0)\\n        \\n        model_A.fit(X_A_boot, y_boot)\\n        model_B.fit(X_B_boot, y_boot)\\n        \\n        # Predict OOB\\n        y_pred_A = model_A.predict(X_A_oob)\\n        y_pred_B = model_B.predict(X_B_oob)\\n        \\n        mse_A = mean_squared_error(y_oob, y_pred_A)\\n        mse_B = mean_squared_error(y_oob, y_pred_B)\\n        \\n        mse_differences.append(mse_A - mse_B)  # Positive = B is better\\n    \\n    # Compute p-value (one-sided: H0 is that B is not better than A)\\n    p_value = np.mean(np.array(mse_differences) <= 0)\\n    \\n    # 95% confidence interval for MSE difference\\n    ci_lower = np.percentile(mse_differences, 2.5)\\n    ci_upper = np.percentile(mse_differences, 97.5)\\n    \\n    # Mean MSE reduction percentage\\n    mse_reduction_pct = (np.mean(mse_differences) / np.mean([mean_squared_error(y, np.zeros_like(y))])) * 100\\n    \\n    return {\\n        'p_value': p_value,\\n        'mse_differences': mse_differences,\\n        'ci_95': (ci_lower, ci_upper),\\n        'mean_mse_reduction_pct': mse_reduction_pct,\\n        'n_significant': np.sum(np.array(mse_differences) > 0)\\n    }\\n\\n# Run for both datasets\\nresults_weebit = paired_bootstrap_test(X_weebit, y_weebit, n_bootstrap=10000)\\nresults_cefr_sp = paired_bootstrap_test(X_cefr, y_cefr, n_bootstrap=10000)\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 2: Bootstrap Standard Errors and 95% CI for Ridge Coefficients\\n\\n```python\\ndef bootstrap_coefficient_ci(X, y, model_type='Ridge', n_bootstrap=10000):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute bootstrap standard errors and 95% CI for model coefficients.\\n    \\n    Approach:\\n    1. ### [42] ASSISTANT · 2026-07-21 15:18:30 UTC

```
The JSON file has been created. Now let me think about whether I need to update the plan with any corrections. Looking at the artifact direction more carefully:

1. The direction mentions "MSE reduction (17.8% WeeBIT, 8.9% CEFR-SP)" - I should make sure the plan computes MSE reduction percentage correctly
2. For effect size, Cohen's d may not be the most appropriate measure for R² improvements. Let me think about what would be better.

Actually, for reporting effect sizes in readability research, it's more common to report:
- The R² difference directly (e.g., "+0.138")
- The percentage improvement in MSE
- Confidence intervals for these improvements

Cohen's d is more appropriate for comparing group means. For R² improvements, we could use:
- The R² difference as the effect size (simple and interpretable)
- Alternatively, convert R² to correlation (r = sqrt(R²)) and compute Cohen's d from that

Let me update the plan to use a more appropriate effect size measure. Also, I realize the plan is quite long and detailed, which is good, but I should verify the JSON is valid and complete.

Let me recreate the file with some improvements - particularly around the effect size calculation and ensuring the output format is clearly specified.

The evaluation addresses five key statistical requirements: (1) paired bootstrap test for MSE reduction significance, (2) bootstrap CI for feature coefficients, (3) proper train/test reporting, (4) effect size analysis, and (5) ablation studies.\\n\\n## Data Loading and Feature Computation\\n\\n```python\\nimport json\\nimport numpy as np\\nimport pandas as pd\\nfrom sklearn.model_selection import cross_val_predict, KFold\\nfrom sklearn.linear_model import Ridge, LinearRegression\\nfrom sklearn.metrics import mean_squared_error, r2_score\\nfrom sklearn.preprocessing import StandardScaler\\nimport scipy.stats as stats\\n\\n# Load datasets\\nwith open('full_data_out.json', 'r') as f:\\n    data = json.load(f)\\n\\n# Extract sentences and readability scores\\n# Dataset format: {\\\"datasets\\\": [{\\\"dataset\\\": \\\"WeeBIT\\\", \\\"examples\\\": [...]}, ...]}\\n\\ndef extract_features(sentences):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute both average and uniformity (CV) features for each sentence.\\n    \\n    Features computed:\\n    - avg_word_length: Mean word length in characters\\n    - avg_syllables: Mean syllable count per word (using CMUdict)\\n    - avg_frequency: Mean word frequency (using SUBTLEX-US or NLTK fallback)\\n    - cv_word_length: Coefficient of variation of word lengths\\n    - cv_syllables: Coefficient of variation of syllable counts\\n    - cv_frequency: Coefficient of variation of word frequencies\\n    - avg_sentence_length: Mean words per sentence (for single sentence, just word count)\\n    \\n    Returns: DataFrame with features for each sentence\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    features_list = []\\n    for sent in sentences:\\n        words = sent.split()\\n        # Word lengths\\n        word_lengths = [len(w) for w in words]\\n        avg_wl = np.mean(word_lengths)\\n        cv_wl = np.std(word_lengths) / (avg_wl + 1e-10)  # Add small epsilon to avoid division by zero\\n        \\n        # Syllable counts (use pronouncing library with CMUdict)\\n        syll_counts = [syllable_count(w) for w in words]  # Implement with CMUdict\\n        avg_syll = np.mean(syll_counts)\\n        cv_syll = np.std(syll_counts) / (avg_syll + 1e-10)\\n        \\n        # Word frequencies (use SUBTLEX-US via NLTK or downloaded file)\\n        freqs = [get_word_frequency(w) for w in words]\\n        avg_freq = np.mean(freqs)\\n        cv_freq = np.std(freqs) / (avg_freq + 1e-10)\\n        \\n        features_list.append({\\n            'avg_word_length': avg_wl,\\n            'avg_syllables': avg_syll,\\n            'avg_frequency': avg_freq,\\n            'cv_word_length': cv_wl,\\n            'cv_syllables': cv_syll,\\n            'cv_frequency': cv_freq,\\n            'sentence_length': len(words)\\n        })\\n    \\n    return pd.DataFrame(features_list)\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 1: Paired Bootstrap Test for MSE Reduction Significance\\n\\n```python\\ndef paired_bootstrap_test(X, y, n_bootstrap=10000):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Test whether adding uniformity features significantly reduces MSE.\\n    \\n    Approach: Paired bootstrap comparing two nested models:\\n    - Model A: Traditional average features only\\n    - Model B: Average + uniformity features\\n    \\n    For each bootstrap sample:\\n    1. Sample indices with replacement (same size as original)\\n    2. Fit both models on bootstrap sample\\n    3. Compute MSE on out-of-bag (OOB) samples\\n    4. Record MSE difference (MSE_A - MSE_B)\\n    \\n    p-value: Proportion of bootstrap samples where MSE_B >= MSE_A\\n    (one-sided test for reduction)\\n    \\n    Returns: p-value, confidence interval for MSE difference\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    n = len(y)\\n    mse_differences = []\\n    \\n    # Feature groupings\\n    avg_features = ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length']\\n    uniformity_features = ['cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency']\\n    \\n    X_avg = X[avg_features]\\n    X_combined = X[avg_features + uniformity_features]\\n    \\n    for b in range(n_bootstrap):\\n        # Bootstrap sample\\n        boot_indices = np.random.choice(n, size=n, replace=True)\\n        oob_indices = np.setdiff1d(np.arange(n), boot_indices)\\n        \\n        if len(oob_indices) == 0:\\n            continue  # Skip if no OOB samples\\n        \\n        # Scale features\\n        scaler_A = StandardScaler()\\n        scaler_B = StandardScaler()\\n        \\n        X_A_boot = scaler_A.fit_transform(X_avg.iloc[boot_indices])\\n        X_A_oob = scaler_A.transform(X_avg.iloc[oob_indices])\\n        \\n        X_B_boot = scaler_B.fit_transform(X_combined.iloc[boot_indices])\\n        X_B_oob = scaler_B.transform(X_combined.iloc[oob_indices])\\n        \\n        y_boot = y[boot_indices]\\n        y_oob = y[oob_indices]\\n        \\n        # Fit models (Ridge for regularization)\\n        model_A = Ridge(alpha=1.0)\\n        model_B = Ridge(alpha=1.0)\\n        \\n        model_A.fit(X_A_boot, y_boot)\\n        model_B.fit(X_B_boot, y_boot)\\n        \\n        # Predict OOB\\n        y_pred_A = model_A.predict(X_A_oob)\\n        y_pred_B = model_B.predict(X_B_oob)\\n        \\n        mse_A = mean_squared_error(y_oob, y_pred_A)\\n        mse_B = mean_squared_error(y_oob, y_pred_B)\\n        \\n        mse_differences.append(mse_A - mse_B)  # Positive = B is better\\n    \\n    # Compute p-value (one-sided: H0 is that B is not better than A)\\n    p_value = np.mean(np.array(mse_differences) <= 0)\\n    \\n    # 95% confidence interval for MSE difference\\n    ci_lower = np.percentile(mse_differences, 2.5)\\n    ci_upper = np.percentile(mse_differences, 97.5)\\n    \\n    # Mean MSE reduction percentage\\n    mse_reduction_pct = (np.mean(mse_differences) / np.mean([mean_squared_error(y, np.zeros_like(y))])) * 100\\n    \\n    return {\\n        'p_value': p_value,\\n        'mse_differences': mse_differences,\\n        'ci_95': (ci_lower, ci_upper),\\n        'mean_mse_reduction_pct': mse_reduction_pct,\\n        'n_significant': np.sum(np.array(mse_differences) > 0)\\n    }\\n\\n# Run for both datasets\\nresults_weebit = paired_bootstrap_test(X_weebit, y_weebit, n_bootstrap=10000)\\nresults_cefr_sp = paired_bootstrap_test(X_cefr, y_cefr, n_bootstrap=10000)\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 2: Bootstrap Standard Errors and 95% CI for Ridge Coefficients\\n\\n```python\\ndef bootstrap_coefficient_ci(X, y, model_type='Ridge', n_bootstrap=10000):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute bootstrap standard errors and 95% CI for model coefficients.\\n    \\n    Approach:\\n    1. For each bootstrap sample, fit the model\\n    2. Store coefficients\\n    3. Compute 2.5th and 97.5th percentiles for each coefficient\\n    4. Coefficients whose CI does not include 0 are statistically significant\\n    \\n    Returns: DataFrame with coefficient, bootstrap SE, 95% CI, p-value\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    n = len(y)\\n    feature_names = X.columns.tolist()\\n    n_features = len(feature_names)\\n    \\n    # Store coefficients from each bootstrap sample\\n    coef_matrix = np.zeros((n_bootstrap, n_features))\\n    intercept_vector = np.zeros(n_bootstrap)\\n    \\n    for b in range(n_bootstrap):\\n        boot_indices = np.random.choice(n, size=n, replace=True)\\n        X_boot = X.iloc[boot_indices]\\n        y_boot = y[boot_indices]\\n        \\n        # Scale features\\n        scaler = StandardScaler()\\n        X_boot_scaled = scaler.fit_transform(X_boot)\\n        \\n        # Fit model\\n        if model_type == 'Ridge':\\n            model = Ridge(alpha=1.0)\\n        else:\\n            model = LinearRegression()\\n        \\n        model.fit(X_boot_scaled, y_boot)\\n        \\n        coef_matrix[b, :] = model.coef_\\n        intercept_vector[b] = model.intercept_\\n    \\n    # Compute statistics\\n    results = []\\n    for i, feature in enumerate(feature_names):\\n        coefs = coef_matrix[:, i]\\n        mean_coef = np.mean(coefs)\\n        std_coef = np.std(coefs)\\n        ci_lower = np.percentile(coefs, 2.5)\\n        ci_upper = np.percentile(coefs, 97.5)\\n        \\n        # Two-sided p-value: proportion of bootstrap samples where coefficient sign differs from mean\\n        if mean_coef >= 0:\\n            p_value = 2 * np.mean(coefs <= 0)\\n        else:\\n            p_value = 2 * np.mean(coefs >= 0)\\n        \\n        results.append({\\n            'feature': feature,\\n            'mean_coefficient': mean_coef,\\n            'bootstrap_se': std_coef,\\n            'ci_95_lower': ci_lower,\\n            'ci_95_upper': ci_upper,\\n            'p_value': p_value,\\n            'significant': (ci_lower > 0) if mean_coef > 0 else (ci_upper < 0)\\n        })\\n    \\n    return pd.DataFrame(results)\\n\\n# Run for combined features model on each dataset\\ncoef_ci_weebit = bootstrap_coefficient_ci(X_weebit_combined, y_weebit, 'Ridge', 10000)\\ncoef_ci_cefr = bootstrap_coefficient_ci(X_cefr_combined, y_cefr, 'Ridge', 10000)\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 3: Proper Train/Test Reporting with Cross-Validation\\n\\n```python\\ndef cross_val_evaluation(X, y, model_type='Ridge', n_splits=5):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Proper cross-validation with clear train/test separation.\\n    Reports ONLY test set metrics (not training metrics).\\n    \\n    Uses K-fold CV where:\\n    - Training fold: used for feature scaling and model fitting\\n    - Test fold: used ONLY for evaluation (no refitting)\\n    \\n    Returns: dict with test set metrics (mean, SD across folds)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    kf = KFold(n_splits=n_splits, shuffle=True, random_state=42)\\n    \\n    test_mse = []\\n    test_r2 = []\\n    test_predictions = []\\n    test_actuals = []\\n    \\n    for train_idx, test_idx in kf.split(X):\\n        X_train, X_test = X.iloc[train_idx], X.iloc[test_idx]\\n        y_train, y_test = y[train_idx], y[test_idx]\\n        \\n        # Scale on training only\\n        scaler = StandardScaler()\\n        X_train_scaled = scaler.fit_transform(X_train)\\n        X_test_scaled = scaler.transform(X_test)\\n        \\n        # Fit on training\\n        if model_type == 'Ridge':\\n            model = Ridge(alpha=1.0)\\n        else:\\n            model = LinearRegression()\\n        \\n        model.fit(X_train_scaled, y_train)\\n        \\n        # Predict test (NO refitting on test)\\n        y_pred = model.predict(X_test_scaled)\\n        \\n        test_mse.append(mean_squared_error(y_test, y_pred))\\n        test_r2.append(r2_score(y_test, y_pred))\\n        test_predictions.extend(y_pred.tolist())\\n        test_actuals.extend(y_test.tolist())\\n    \\n    return {\\n        'test_mse_mean': np.mean(test_mse),\\n        'test_mse_sd': np.std(test_mse),\\n        'test_mse_folds': test_mse,\\n        'test_r2_mean': np.mean(test_r2),\\n        'test_r2_sd': np.std(test_r2),\\n        'test_r2_folds': test_r2,\\n        'test_predictions': test_predictions,\\n        'test_actuals': test_actuals\\n    }\\n\\n# Evaluate three model variants\\nmodels_to_evaluate = {\\n    'average_only': ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length'],\\n    'uniformity_only': ['cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency'],\\n    'combined': ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length',\\n                 'cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency']\\n}\\n\\nresults = {}\\nfor model_name, features in models_to_evaluate.items():\\n    X_subset = X[features]\\n    results[model_name] = cross_val_evaluation(X_subset, y, 'Ridge', 5)\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 4: Effect Size Analysis (Cohen's d for R\u00b2 Improvements)\\n\\n```python\\ndef cohens_d_r2_improvement(r2_A, r2_B, n):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute Cohen's d for R\u00b2 improvement from model A to model B.\\n    \\n    Approach: Treat R\u00b2 as a correlation-like effect size.\\n    Cohen's d for correlation: d = 2*r / sqrt(1 - r^2)\\n    where r = sqrt(R\u00b2)\\n    \\n    For R\u00b2 improvement: Compare the correlations\\n    r_A = sqrt(R\u00b2_A), r_B = sqrt(R\u00b2_B)\\n    \\n    Alternative: Use Cohen's d for independent samples on R\u00b2 values\\n    (if we have R\u00b2 from multiple CV folds, treat as independent measurements)\\n    \\n    Returns: Cohen's d, interpretation ('small', 'medium', 'large')\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Method 1: If we have R\u00b2 from multiple CV folds\\n    # Treat as two sets of independent measurements\\n    mean_A, sd_A = np.mean(r2_A), np.std(r2_A)\\n    mean_B, sd_B = np.mean(r2_B), np.std(r2_B)\\n    n_A = n_B = len(r2_A)\\n    \\n    # Pooled standard deviation\\n    s_pooled = np.sqrt(((n_A - 1) * sd_A**2 + (n_B - 1) * sd_B**2) / (n_A + n_B - 2))\\n    \\n    # Cohen's d\\n    d = (mean_B - mean_A) / s_pooled\\n    \\n    # Interpretation\\n    if abs(d) < 0.2:\\n        interpretation = 'negligible'\\n    elif abs(d) < 0.5:\\n        interpretation = 'small'\\n    elif abs(d) < 0.8:\\n        interpretation = 'medium'\\n    else:\\n        interpretation = 'large'\\n    \\n    return {\\n        'cohens_d': d,\\n        'interpretation': interpretation,\\n        'mean_r2_A': mean_A,\\n        'mean_r2_B': mean_B,\\n        'r2_improvement': mean_B - mean_A\\n    }\\n\\n# Compute for both datasets\\neffect_size_weebit = cohens_d_r2_improvement(\\n    results['average_only']['test_r2_folds'],\\n    results['combined']['test_r2_folds'],\\n    len(y_weebit)\\n)\\n\\neffect_size_cefr = cohens_d_r2_improvement(\\n    results['average_only']['test_r2_folds'],\\n    results['combined']['test_r2_folds'],\\n    len(y_cefr)\\n)\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 5: Ablation Study - Test Each Uniformity Feature Individually\\n\\n```python\\ndef ablation_study(X, y):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Test each uniformity feature individually to identify unique contributions.\\n    \\n    Approach: For each uniformity feature, create a model with:\\n    - All average features + one uniformity feature\\n    \\n    Compare R\u00b2 to average-only baseline.\\n    \\n    Also test: removing one uniformity feature at a time from combined model\\n    to see which causes largest R\u00b2 drop.\\n    \\n    Returns: DataFrame with R\u00b2 for each ablation condition\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    avg_features = ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length']\\n    uniformity_features = ['cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency']\\n    \\n    ablation_results = []\\n    \\n    # Baseline: average only\\n    baseline = cross_val_evaluation(X[avg_features], y, 'Ridge', 5)\\n    ablation_results.append({\\n        'condition': 'average_only',\\n        'features': avg_features,\\n        'test_r2_mean': baseline['test_r2_mean'],\\n        'test_r2_sd': baseline['test_r2_sd']\\n    })\\n    \\n    # Add one uniformity feature at a time\\n    for uf in uniformity_features:\\n        features = avg_features + [uf]\\n        result = cross_val_evaluation(X[features], y, 'Ridge', 5)\\n        ablation_results.append({\\n            'condition': f'average + {uf}',\\n            'features': features,\\n            'test_r2_mean': result['test_r2_mean'],\\n            'test_r2_sd': result['test_r2_sd'],\\n            'r2_improvement': result['test_r2_mean'] - baseline['test_r2_mean']\\n        })\\n    \\n    # Full combined\\n    combined_features = avg_features + uniformity_features\\n    combined_result = cross_val_evaluation(X[combined_features], y, 'Ridge', 5)\\n    ablation_results.append({\\n        'condition': 'combined (all features)',\\n        'features': combined_features,\\n        'test_r2_mean': combined_result['test_r2_mean'],\\n        'test_r2_sd': combined_result['test_r2_sd'],\\n        'r2_improvement': combined_result['test_r2_mean'] - baseline['test_r2_mean']\\n    })\\n    \\n    # Removal ablation: remove one at a time from combined\\n    for uf in uniformity_features:\\n        features = [f for f in combined_features if f != uf]\\n        result = cross_val_evaluation(X[features], y, 'Ridge', 5)\\n        ablation_results.append({\\n            'condition': f'combined without {uf}',\\n            'features': features,\\n            'test_r2_mean': result['test_r2_mean'],\\n            'test_r2_sd': result['test_r2_sd'],\\n            'r2_drop': combined_result['test_r2_mean'] - result['test_r2_mean']\\n        })\\n    \\n    return pd.DataFrame(ablation_results)\\n\\nablation_weebit = ablation_study(X_weebit, y_weebit)\\nablation_cefr = ablation_study(X_cefr, y_cefr)\\n```\\n\\n## Output Generation\\n\\n```python\\ndef generate_publication_tables(results_dict):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Generate publication-ready tables with mean, SD, CI for all metrics.\\n    \\n    Tables to generate:\\n    1. Table 1: Cross-validated test set performance (average-only, uniformity-only, combined)\\n    2. Table 2: Bootstrap CI for Ridge coefficients (which features are significant)\\n    3. Table 3: Ablation study results\\n    4. Table 4: Effect size analysis (Cohen's d)\\n    5. Table 5: Paired bootstrap test results (MSE reduction significance)\\n    \\n    All tables include: mean, SD, 95% CI, p-values where applicable\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    tables = {}\\n    \\n    # Table 1: Model performance comparison\\n    table1 = []\\n    for model_name in ['average_only', 'uniformity_only', 'combined']:\\n        r = results_dict[model_name]\\n        table1.append({\\n            'Model': model_name,\\n            'Test R\u00b2 (mean)': f\\\"{r['test_r2_mean']:.4f}\\\",\\n            'Test R\u00b2 (SD)': f\\\"{r['test_r2_sd']:.4f}\\\",\\n            'Test MSE (mean)': f\\\"{r['test_mse_mean']:.4f}\\\",\\n            'Test MSE (SD)': f\\\"{r['test_mse_sd']:.4f}\\\"\\n        })\\n    tables['table1_model_performance'] = table1\\n    \\n    # Table 2: Coefficient significance\\n    tables['table2_coefficient_ci'] = coef_ci_results  # From Experiment 2\\n    \\n    # Table 3: Ablation\\n    tables['table3_ablation'] = ablation_results  # From Experiment 5\\n    \\n    # Table 4: Effect size\\n    tables['table4_effect_size'] = effect_size_results  # From Experiment 4\\n    \\n    # Table 5: Bootstrap test for MSE reduction\\n    tables['table5_mse_reduction_test'] = bootstrap_test_results  # From Experiment 1\\n    \\n    # Save all tables to JSON\\n    with open('method_out.json', 'w') as f:\\n        json.dump(tables, f, indent=2)\\n    \\n    # Also save as CSV for easy inspection\\n    for table_name, table_data in tables.items():\\n        if isinstance(table_data, list):\\n            pd.DataFrame(table_data).to_csv(f'{table_name}.csv', index=False)\\n    \\n    return tables\\n```\\n\\n## Execution Timeline (6 hours)\\n\\n```\\nHour 0-1: Data loading and feature computation\\n- Load full_data_out.json\\n- Implement syllable counting with CMUdict (pronouncing library)\\n- Implement word frequency lookup (SUBTLEX-US or NLTK)\\n- Compute all features for 13,129 sentences\\n- Save computed features to features.pkl for reuse\\n\\nHour 1-2: Experiment 1 (Bootstrap test for MSE reduction)\\n- Implement paired bootstrap test\\n- Run 10,000 bootstrap samples for both datasets\\n- Compute p-values and confidence intervals\\n\\nHour 2-3: Experiment 2 (Bootstrap CI for coefficients)\\n- Implement bootstrap coefficient CI\\n- Run 10,000 bootstrap samples for both datasets\\n- Identify significant features\\n\\nHour 3-4: Experiment 3 (Proper CV evaluation)\\n- Implement proper cross-validation\\n- Evaluate all three model variants\\n- Generate test set metrics only\\n\\nHour 4-5: Experiment 4-5 (Effect size + Ablation)\\n- Compute Cohen's d for R\u00b2 improvements\\n- Run ablation studies\\n\\nHour 5-6: Output generation and validation\\n- Generate publication-ready tables\\n- Validate results (check for obvious errors)\\n- Save all results to method_out.json\\n```\"",
  "new_str": "\"implementation_pseudocode\": \"## Overview\\n\\nThis experiment conducts comprehensive statistical evaluation of the Uniformity Principle hypothesis using the WeeBIT and CEFR-SP datasets (13,129 sentences total). The evaluation addresses five key statistical requirements: (1) paired bootstrap test for MSE reduction significance, (2) bootstrap CI for feature coefficients, (3) proper train/test reporting, (4) effect size analysis, and (5) ablation studies.\\n\\n**Key Statistical Approaches**:\\n- Bootstrap hypothesis testing (10,000 samples) for MSE reduction significance\\n- Bootstrap percentile confidence intervals for Ridge regression coefficients\\n- 5-fold cross-validation with proper train/test separation (reporting test metrics only)\\n- Effect size: R\u00b2 improvement with 95% CI, and Cohen's d for practical significance\\n- Ablation: add-one-in and remove-one-out uniformity feature analysis\\n\\n## Data Loading and Feature Computation\\n\\n```python\\nimport json\\nimport numpy as np\\nimport pandas as pd\\nfrom sklearn.model_selection import KFold\\nfrom sklearn.linear_model import Ridge\\nfrom sklearn.metrics import mean_squared_error, r2_score\\nfrom sklearn.preprocessing import StandardScaler\\nimport scipy.stats as stats\\nimport pronouncing  # For CMUdict syllable counting\\n\\n# Load datasets from dependency artifact\\ndef load_datasets():\\n    with open('full_data_out.json', 'r') as f:\\n        data = json.load(f)\\n    \\n    sentences = []\\n    scores = []\\n    sources = []\\n    \\n    for dataset in data['datasets']:\\n        for example in dataset['examples']:\\n            sentences.append(example['input'])\\n            # Convert output to float (readability score, normalized 0-1)\\n            scores.append(float(example['output']))\\n            sources.append(dataset['dataset'])\\n    \\n    return sentences, np.array(scores), np.array(sources)\\n\\nsentences, y, sources = load_datasets()\\nprint(f\\\"Loaded {len(sentences)} sentences\\\")\\nprint(f\\\"WeeBIT: {np.sum(sources == 'WeeBIT')}, CEFR-SP: {np.sum(sources == 'CEFR-SP')}\\\")\\n\\ndef syllable_count(word):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Count syllables using CMUdict, with heuristic fallback.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    word = word.lower().strip('.,!?;:')\\n    phones = pronouncing.phones_for_word(word)\\n    if phones:\\n        return pronouncing.syllable_count(phones[0])\\n    else:\\n        # Heuristic fallback: count vowel groups\\n        vowels = 'aeiouy'\\n        count = 0\\n        prev_was_vowel = False\\n        for char in word:\\n            is_vowel = char in vowels\\n            if is_vowel and not prev_was_vowel:\\n                count += 1\\n            prev_was_vowel = is_vowel\\n        if word.endswith('e'):\\n            count = max(1, count - 1)\\n        return max(1, count)\\n\\ndef get_word_frequency(word):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Get word frequency using SUBTLEX-US norms or NLTK fallback.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Implementation: load SUBTLEX-US data from file or use NLTK frequencies\\n    # Return log frequency (higher = more frequent = easier)\\n    pass  # Detailed implementation in executor\\n\\ndef extract_features(sentences):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute both average and uniformity (CV) features for each sentence.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    features_list = []\\n    for sent in sentences:\\n        words = [w for w in sent.split() if w]  # Remove empty strings\\n        if len(words) == 0:\\n            features_list.append({f: 0.0 for f in ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', \\n                                                      'cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency',\\n                                                      'sentence_length']})\\n            continue\\n        \\n        # Word lengths\\n        word_lengths = np.array([len(w) for w in words])\\n        avg_wl = np.mean(word_lengths)\\n        cv_wl = np.std(word_lengths) / (avg_wl + 1e-10)\\n        \\n        # Syllable counts\\n        syll_counts = np.array([syllable_count(w) for w in words])\\n        avg_syll = np.mean(syll_counts)\\n        cv_syll = np.std(syll_counts) / (avg_syll + 1e-10)\\n        \\n        # Word frequencies\\n        freqs = np.array([get_word_frequency(w) for w in words])\\n        avg_freq = np.mean(freqs)\\n        cv_freq = np.std(freqs) / (avg_freq + 1e-10)\\n        \\n        features_list.append({\\n            'avg_word_length': avg_wl,\\n            'avg_syllables': avg_syll,\\n            'avg_frequency': avg_freq,\\n            'cv_word_length': cv_wl,\\n            'cv_syllables': cv_syll,\\n            'cv_frequency': cv_freq,\\n            'sentence_length': len(words)\\n        })\\n    \\n    return pd.DataFrame(features_list)\\n\\nX = extract_features(sentences)\\nprint(f\\\"Features shape: {X.shape}\\\")\\nprint(f\\\"Any NaN? {X.isnull().any().any()}\\\")\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 1: Paired Bootstrap Test for MSE Reduction Significance\\n\\n```python\\ndef paired_bootstrap_mse_test(X, y, n_bootstrap=10000, random_state=42):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Paired bootstrap test for whether adding uniformity features reduces MSE.\\n    \\n    H0: Adding uniformity features does NOT reduce MSE (MSE_combined >= MSE_average)\\n    H1: Adding uniformity features reduces MSE (MSE_combined < MSE_average)\\n    \\n    Approach (out-of-bag bootstrap):\\n    1. For each bootstrap iteration b:\\n       - Sample n indices with replacement from [0, n-1]\\n       - Fit Model A (average features) and Model B (combined) on bootstrap sample\\n       - Predict on out-of-bag (OOB) samples\\n       - Compute MSE_A and MSE_B on OOB\\n       - Record: mse_diff = MSE_A - MSE_B (positive = B better)\\n    \\n    2. One-sided p-value = proportion of bootstrap samples where mse_diff <= 0\\n       (i.e., proportion where B is NOT better)\\n    \\n    3. 95% CI for MSE difference = [2.5 percentile, 97.5 percentile] of mse_differences\\n    \\n    4. MSE reduction % = (mean(mse_differences) / MSE_baseline) * 100\\n    \\n    Returns: dict with p_value, ci_95, mse_reduction_pct, mse_differences\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    np.random.seed(random_state)\\n    n = len(y)\\n    \\n    avg_features = ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length']\\n    uniformity_features = ['cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency']\\n    combined_features = avg_features + uniformity_features\\n    \\n    mse_differences = []\\n    \\n    for b in range(n_bootstrap):\\n        # Bootstrap sample\\n        boot_idx = np.random.choice(n, size=n, replace=True)\\n        oob_idx = np.setdiff1d(np.arange(n), boot_idx)\\n        \\n        if len(oob_idx) < 10:  # Need at least 10 OOB samples\\n            continue\\n        \\n        # Scale features per bootstrap sample\\n        scaler_A = StandardScaler()\\n        scaler_B = StandardScaler()\\n        \\n        X_A_boot = scaler_A.fit_transform(X.loc[boot_idx, avg_features])\\n        X_A_oob = scaler_A.transform(X.loc[oob_idx, avg_features])\\n        \\n        X_B_boot = scaler_B.fit_transform(X.loc[boot_idx, combined_features])\\n        X_B_oob = scaler_B.transform(X.loc[oob_idx, combined_features])\\n        \\n        y_boot = y[boot_idx]\\n        y_oob = y[oob_idx]\\n        \\n        # Fit models\\n        model_A = Ridge(alpha=1.0, random_state=42)\\n        model_B = Ridge(alpha=1.0, random_state=42)\\n        \\n        model_A.fit(X_A_boot, y_boot)\\n        model_B.fit(X_B_boot, y_boot)\\n        \\n        # MSE on OOB\\n        mse_A = mean_squared_error(y_oob, model_A.predict(X_A_oob))\\n        mse_B = mean_squared_error(y_oob, model_B.predict(X_B_oob))\\n        \\n        mse_differences.append(mse_A - mse_B)  # Positive = combined model better\\n    \\n    mse_differences = np.array(mse_differences)\\n    \\n    # One-sided p-value (H1: B reduces MSE compared to A)\\n    # p = P(MSE_B >= MSE_A) under H0\\n    p_value = np.mean(mse_differences <= 0)\\n    \\n    # Two-sided p-value also reported\\n    p_value_two_sided = 2 * min(p_value, 1 - p_value)\\n    \\n    # 95% CI for MSE difference\\n    ci_lower = np.percentile(mse_differences, 2.5)\\n    ci_upper = np.percentile(mse_differences, 97.5)\\n    \\n    # MSE reduction percentage\\n    mse_baseline = np.mean([mean_squared_error(y, np.full_like(y, np.mean(y)))])\\n    mean_mse_reduction = np.mean(mse_differences)\\n    mse_reduction_pct = (mean_mse_reduction / mse_baseline) * 100\\n    \\n    return {\\n        'p_value_one_sided': p_value,\\n        'p_value_two_sided': p_value_two_sided,\\n        'mse_differences': mse_differences.tolist(),\\n        'ci_95_lower': ci_lower,\\n        'ci_95_upper': ci_upper,\\n        'mean_mse_reduction': mean_mse_reduction,\\n        'mse_reduction_pct': mse_reduction_pct,\\n        'n_valid_bootstrap': len(mse_differences)\\n    }\\n\\n# Run on both datasets\\nresults_weebit = paired_bootstrap_mse_test(X[sources == 'WeeBIT'], y[sources == 'WeeBIT'], 10000)\\nresults_cefr = paired_bootstrap_mse_test(X[sources == 'CEFR-SP'], y[sources == 'CEFR-SP'], 10000)\\n\\nprint(f\\\"WeeBIT: MSE reduction = {results_weebit['mse_reduction_pct']:.2f}%, p = {results_weebit['p_value_one_sided']:.4f}\\\")\\nprint(f\\\"CEFR-SP: MSE reduction = {results_cefr['mse_reduction_pct']:.2f}%, p = {results_cefr['p_value_one_sided']:.4f}\\\")\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 2: Bootstrap CI for Ridge Regression Coefficients\\n\\n```python\\ndef bootstrap_coefficient_ci(X, y, n_bootstrap=10000, alpha=0.05, random_state=42):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Bootstrap confidence intervals for model coefficients.\\n    \\n    Approach:\\n    1. For each bootstrap sample, fit Ridge regression\\n    2. Store coefficients\\n    3. Compute percentile CI (default 95%)\\n    4. Check if CI excludes 0 (statistical significance)\\n    \\n    Also computes bootstrap standard error and z-statistic p-value.\\n    \\n    Returns: DataFrame with feature, coef, bootstrap_se, ci_lower, ci_upper, p_value, significant\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    np.random.seed(random_state)\\n    n = len(y)\\n    feature_names = X.columns.tolist()\\n    n_features = len(feature_names)\\n    \\n    coef_matrix = np.zeros((n_bootstrap, n_features))\\n    intercept_vector = np.zeros(n_bootstrap)\\n    \\n    for b in range(n_bootstrap):\\n        boot_idx = np.random.choice(n, size=n, replace=True)\\n        \\n        scaler = StandardScaler()\\n        X_boot = scaler.fit_transform(X.iloc[boot_idx])\\n        y_boot = y[boot_idx]\\n        \\n        model = Ridge(alpha=1.0, random_state=42)\\n        model.fit(X_boot, y_boot)\\n        \\n        coef_matrix[b, :] = model.coef_\\n        intercept_vector[b] = model.intercept_\\n    \\n    # Compute statistics\\n    results = []\\n    for i, feature in enumerate(feature_names):\\n        coefs = coef_matrix[:, i]\\n        mean_coef = np.mean(coefs)\\n        bootstrap_se = np.std(coefs)\\n        \\n        # Percentile CI\\n        lower = np.percentile(coefs, (alpha/2) * 100)\\n        upper = np.percentile(coefs, (1 - alpha/2) * 100)\\n        \\n        # P-value: proportion of bootstrap samples where coefficient sign differs from mean\\n        if mean_coef >= 0:\\n            p_val = 2 * np.mean(coefs <= 0)\\n        else:\\n            p_val = 2 * np.mean(coefs >= 0)\\n        \\n        # Significance: CI does not include 0\\n        significant = (lower > 0) if mean_coef > 0 else (upper < 0)\\n        \\n        results.append({\\n            'feature': feature,\\n            'mean_coefficient': mean_coef,\\n            'bootstrap_se': bootstrap_se,\\n            'ci_95_lower': lower,\\n            'ci_95_upper': upper,\\n            'p_value': p_val,\\n            'significant': significant\\n        })\\n    \\n    return pd.DataFrame(results)\\n\\n# Run on combined features model\\nX_combined = X[['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length',\\n                'cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency']]\\n\\ncoef_ci_weebit = bootstrap_coefficient_ci(X_combined[sources == 'WeeBIT'], y[sources == 'WeeBIT'], 10000)\\ncoef_ci_cefr = bootstrap_coefficient_ci(X_combined[sources == 'CEFR-SP'], y[sources == 'CEFR-SP'], 10000)\\n\\nprint(\\\"WeeBIT coefficient significance:\\\")\\nprint(coef_ci_weebit[coef_ci_weebit['significant']][['feature', 'mean_coefficient', 'ci_95_lower', 'ci_95_upper']])\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 3: Proper Cross-Validation with Train/Test Separation\\n\\n```python\\ndef cross_val_evaluation(X, y, model_type='Ridge', n_splits=5, random_state=42):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Proper cross-validation with clear train/test separation.\\n    **Only test set metrics are reported** (training metrics are NOT reported\\n    to avoid optimistic bias).\\n    \\n    Uses sklearn KFold with shuffle=True.\\n    \\n    Returns: dict with test set metrics (mean, SD, per-fold values)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    kf = KFold(n_splits=n_splits, shuffle=True, random_state=random_state)\\n    \\n    test_mse_folds = []\\n    test_r2_folds = []\\n    test_mae_folds = []\\n    all_predictions = []\\n    all_actuals = []\\n    \\n    for fold, (train_idx, test_idx) in enumerate(kf.split(X)):\\n        X_train, X_test = X.iloc[train_idx], X.iloc[test_idx]\\n        y_train, y_test = y[train_idx], y[test_idx]\\n        \\n        # Scale on training, apply to test\\n        scaler = StandardScaler()\\n        X_train_scaled = scaler.fit_transform(X_train)\\n        X_test_scaled = scaler.transform(X_test)\\n        \\n        # Fit on training\\n        if model_type == 'Ridge':\\n            model = Ridge(alpha=1.0, random_state=42)\\n        else:\\n            model = LinearRegression()\\n        \\n        model.fit(X_train_scaled, y_train)\\n        \\n        # Predict test (NO refitting on test!)\\n        y_pred = model.predict(X_test_scaled)\\n        \\n        # Test metrics only\\n        test_mse_folds.append(mean_squared_error(y_test, y_pred))\\n        test_r2_folds.append(r2_score(y_test, y_pred))\\n        test_mae_folds.append(np.mean(np.abs(y_test - y_pred)))\\n        \\n        all_predictions.extend(y_pred.tolist())\\n        all_actuals.extend(y_test.tolist())\\n        \\n        print(f\\\"  Fold {fold+1}: Test R\u00b2 = {test_r2_folds[-1]:.4f}, Test MSE = {test_mse_folds[-1]:.4f}\\\")\\n    \\n    return {\\n        'test_mse_mean': np.mean(test_mse_folds),\\n        'test_mse_sd': np.std(test_mse_folds),\\n        'test_mse_folds': test_mse_folds,\\n        'test_r2_mean': np.mean(test_r2_folds),\\n        'test_r2_sd': np.std(test_r2_folds),\\n        'test_r2_folds': test_r2_folds,\\n        'test_mae_mean': np.mean(test_mae_folds),\\n        'test_mae_sd': np.std(test_mae_folds),\\n        'test_predictions': all_predictions,\\n        'test_actuals': all_actuals\\n    }\\n\\n# Evaluate three model variants\\nmodels_to_evaluate = {\\n    'average_only': ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length'],\\n    'uniformity_only': ['cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency'],\\n    'combined': ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length',\\n                 'cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency']\\n}\\n\\ncv_results = {}\\nfor model_name, features in models_to_evaluate.items():\\n    print(f\\\"\\\\nEvaluating: {model_name}\\\")\\n    cv_results[model_name] = cross_val_evaluation(X[features], y, 'Ridge', 5)\\n    \\n# Print comparison table\\nprint(\\\"\\\\n\\\" + \\\"=\\\"*60)\\nprint(\\\"CROSS-VALIDATED TEST SET PERFORMANCE (mean \u00b1 SD)\\\")\\nprint(\\\"=\\\"*60)\\nfor model_name in ['average_only', 'uniformity_only', 'combined']:\\n    r = cv_results[model_name]\\n    print(f\\\"{model_name:20s}: R\u00b2 = {r['test_r2_mean']:.4f} \u00b1 {r['test_r2_sd']:.4f}, \\\"\\n          f\\\"MSE = {r['test_mse_mean']:.4f} \u00b1 {r['test_mse_sd']:.4f}\\\")\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 4: Effect Size Analysis\\n\\n```python\\ndef compute_effect_sizes(cv_results, n):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute effect sizes for R\u00b2 improvements.\\n    \\n    Approach 1: R\u00b2 difference as effect size (simple, interpretable)\\n    - Report: mean R\u00b2 difference, 95% bootstrap CI for difference\\n    \\n    Approach 2: Cohen's d for R\u00b2 improvement\\n    - Convert R\u00b2 to correlation: r = sqrt(R\u00b2)\\n    - Compute Cohen's d for the correlation difference\\n    - Interpretation: d = 0.2 (small), 0.5 (medium), 0.8 (large)\\n    \\n    Approach 3: Practical significance via R\u00b2 classification (Cohen, 1988)\\n    - R\u00b2 = 0.01 (small), 0.09 (medium), 0.25 (large)\\n    \\n    Returns: dict with effect size measures\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    r2_avg = np.array(cv_results['average_only']['test_r2_folds'])\\n    r2_combined = np.array(cv_results['combined']['test_r2_folds'])\\n    \\n    # R\u00b2 difference\\n    r2_diff = r2_combined - r2_avg\\n    mean_diff = np.mean(r2_diff)\\n    sd_diff = np.std(r2_diff)\\n    \\n    # Bootstrap CI for R\u00b2 difference\\n    n_folds = len(r2_diff)\\n    r2_diff_boot = []\\n    for b in range(10000):\\n        idx = np.random.choice(n_folds, n_folds, replace=True)\\n        r2_diff_boot.append(np.mean(r2_combined[idx] - r2_avg[idx]))\\n    ci_lower = np.percentile(r2_diff_boot, 2.5)\\n    ci_upper = np.percentile(r2_diff_boot, 97.5)\\n    \\n    # Cohen's d for R\u00b2 improvement (using correlation conversion)\\n    # Convert R\u00b2 to correlation, then compute d from correlation\\n    r_avg = np.sqrt(np.maximum(r2_avg, 0))  # Avoid negative R\u00b2\\n    r_combined = np.sqrt(np.maximum(r2_combined, 0))\\n    \\n    # Cohen's d from correlation: d = 2r / sqrt(1 - r^2)\\n    # Compute for each fold, then average\\n    d_values = []\\n    for r_a, r_c in zip(r_avg, r_combined):\\n        if r_a < 1 and r_c < 1:\\n            d_a = 2 * r_a / np.sqrt(1 - r_a**2 + 1e-10)\\n            d_c = 2 * r_c / np.sqrt(1 - r_c**2 + 1e-10)\\n            d_values.append(d_c - d_a)  # Difference in d\\n    \\n    cohens_d = np.mean(d_values) if d_values else 0.0\\n    \\n    # Interpretation\\n    abs_d = abs(cohens_d)\\n    if abs_d < 0.2:\\n        interpretation = 'negligible'\\n    elif abs_d < 0.5:\\n        interpretation = 'small'\\n    elif abs_d < 0.8:\\n        interpretation = 'medium'\\n    else:\\n        interpretation = 'large'\\n    \\n    # Percentage variance explained gained\\n    pct_improvement = (mean_diff / np.mean(r2_avg)) * 100 if np.mean(r2_avg) > 0 else 0\\n    \\n    return {\\n        'r2_difference_mean': mean_diff,\\n        'r2_difference_sd': sd_diff,\\n        'r2_difference_ci_95': (ci_lower, ci_upper),\\n        'cohens_d': cohens_d,\\n        'cohens_d_interpretation': interpretation,\\n        'mse_reduction_pct': (1 - np.mean(r2_combined) / np.mean(r2_avg)) * 100,  # Approximate\\n        'practical_significance': 'large' if mean_diff > 0.05 else ('medium' if mean_diff > 0.02 else 'small')\\n    }\\n\\neffect_sizes_weebit = compute_effect_sizes(\\n    {k: {fold: cv_results[k]['test_r2_folds'][i] for i in range(5)} for k in cv_results},\\n    len(y[sources == 'WeeBIT'])\\n)\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 5: Ablation Study\\n\\n```python\\ndef ablation_study(X, y, n_splits=5):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Ablation study: test each uniformity feature individually.\\n    \\n    Design:\\n    (A) Add-one-in: Start with average features, add one uniformity feature at a time\\n    (B) Remove-one-out: Start with combined features, remove one uniformity feature at a time\\n    \\n    Returns: DataFrame with R\u00b2 for each ablation condition\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    avg_features = ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length']\\n    uniformity_features = ['cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency']\\n    \\n    results = []\\n    \\n    # Baseline: average only\\n    baseline = cross_val_evaluation(X[avg_features], y, 'Ridge', n_splits)\\n    results.append({\\n        'condition': 'average_only (baseline)',\\n        'features_used': avg_features,\\n        'test_r2_mean': baseline['test_r2_mean'],\\n        'test_r2_sd': baseline['test_r2_sd'],\\n        'r2_above_baseline': 0.0\\n    })\\n    \\n    # Add-one-in ablation\\n    for uf in uniformity_features:\\n        features = avg_features + [uf]\\n        result = cross_val_evaluation(X[features], y, 'Ridge', n_splits)\\n        results.append({\\n            'condition': f'average + {uf}',\\n            'features_used': features,\\n            'test_r2_mean': result['test_r2_mean'],\\n            'test_r2_sd': result['test_r2_sd'],\\n            'r2_above_baseline': result['test_r2_mean'] - baseline['test_r2_mean']\\n        })\\n    \\n    # Full combined\\n    combined_features = For each bootstrap iteration b:\\n       - Sample n indices with replacement from [0, n-1]\\n       - Fit Model A (average features) and Model B (combined) on bootstrap sample\\n       - Predict on out-of-bag (OOB) samples\\n       - Compute MSE_A and MSE_B on OOB\\n       - Record: mse_diff = MSE_A - MSE_B (positive = B better)\\n    \\n    2. One-sided p-value = proportion of bootstrap samples where mse_diff <= 0\\n       (i.e., proportion where B is NOT better)\\n    \\n    3. 95% CI for MSE difference = [2.5 percentile, 97.5 percentile] of mse_differences\\n    \\n    4.
