Heuristic fallback: count vowel groups\\n        vowels = 'aeiouy'\\n        count = 0\\n        prev_was_vowel = False\\n        for char in word:\\n            is_vowel = char in vowels\\n            if is_vowel and not prev_was_vowel:\\n                count += 1\\n            prev_was_vowel = is_vowel\\n        if word.endswith('e'):\\n            count = max(1, count - 1)\\n        return max(1, count)\\n\\ndef get_word_frequency(word):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Get word frequency using SUBTLEX-US norms or NLTK fallback.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Implementation: load SUBTLEX-US data from file or use NLTK frequencies\\n    # Return log frequency (higher = more frequent = easier)\\n    pass  # Detailed implementation in executor\\n\\ndef extract_features(sentences):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute both average and uniformity (CV) features for each sentence.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    features_list = []\\n    for sent in sentences:\\n        words = [w for w in sent.split() if w]  # Remove empty strings\\n        if len(words) == 0:\\n            features_list.append({f: 0.0 for f in ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', \\n                                                      'cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency',\\n                                                      'sentence_length']})\\n            continue\\n        \\n        # Word lengths\\n        word_lengths = np.array([len(w) for w in words])\\n        avg_wl = np.mean(word_lengths)\\n        cv_wl = np.std(word_lengths) / (avg_wl + 1e-10)\\n        \\n        # Syllable counts\\n        syll_counts = np.array([syllable_count(w) for w in words])\\n        avg_syll = np.mean(syll_counts)\\n        cv_syll = np.std(syll_counts) / (avg_syll + 1e-10)\\n        \\n        # Word frequencies\\n        freqs = np.array([get_word_frequency(w) for w in words])\\n        avg_freq = np.mean(freqs)\\n        cv_freq = np.std(freqs) / (avg_freq + 1e-10)\\n        \\n        features_list.append({\\n            'avg_word_length': avg_wl,\\n            'avg_syllables': avg_syll,\\n            'avg_frequency': avg_freq,\\n            'cv_word_length': cv_wl,\\n            'cv_syllables': cv_syll,\\n            'cv_frequency': cv_freq,\\n            'sentence_length': len(words)\\n        })\\n    \\n    return pd.DataFrame(features_list)\\n\\nX = extract_features(sentences)\\nprint(f\\\"Features shape: {X.shape}\\\")\\nprint(f\\\"Any NaN? {X.isnull().any().any()}\\\")\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 1: Paired Bootstrap Test for MSE Reduction Significance\\n\\n```python\\ndef paired_bootstrap_mse_test(X, y, n_bootstrap=10000, random_state=42):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Paired bootstrap test for whether adding uniformity features reduces MSE.\\n    \\n    H0: Adding uniformity features does NOT reduce MSE (MSE_combined >= MSE_average)\\n    H1: Adding uniformity features reduces MSE (MSE_combined < MSE_average)\\n    \\n    Approach (out-of-bag bootstrap):\\n    1. For each bootstrap iteration b:\\n       - Sample n indices with replacement from [0, n-1]\\n       - Fit Model A (average features) and Model B (combined) on bootstrap sample\\n       - Predict on out-of-bag (OOB) samples\\n       - Compute MSE_A and MSE_B on OOB\\n       - Record: mse_diff = MSE_A - MSE_B (positive = B better)\\n    \\n    2. One-sided p-value = proportion of bootstrap samples where mse_diff <= 0\\n       (i.e., proportion where B is NOT better)\\n    \\n    3. 95% CI for MSE difference = [2.5 percentile, 97.5 percentile] of mse_differences\\n    \\n    4. MSE reduction % = (mean(mse_differences) / MSE_baseline) * 100\\n    \\n    Returns: dict with p_value, ci_95, mse_reduction_pct, mse_differences\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    np.random.seed(random_state)\\n    n = len(y)\\n    \\n    avg_features = ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length']\\n    uniformity_features = ['cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency']\\n    combined_features = avg_features + uniformity_features\\n    \\n    mse_differences = []\\n    \\n    for b in range(n_bootstrap):\\n        # Bootstrap sample\\n        boot_idx = np.random.choice(n, size=n, replace=True)\\n        oob_idx = np.setdiff1d(np.arange(n), boot_idx)\\n        \\n        if len(oob_idx) < 10:  # Need at least 10 OOB samples\\n            continue\\n        \\n        # Scale features per bootstrap sample\\n        scaler_A = StandardScaler()\\n        scaler_B = StandardScaler()\\n        \\n        X_A_boot = scaler_A.fit_transform(X.loc[boot_idx, avg_features])\\n        X_A_oob = scaler_A.transform(X.loc[oob_idx, avg_features])\\n        \\n        X_B_boot = scaler_B.fit_transform(X.loc[boot_idx, combined_features])\\n        X_B_oob = scaler_B.transform(X.loc[oob_idx, combined_features])\\n        \\n        y_boot = y[boot_idx]\\n        y_oob = y[oob_idx]\\n        \\n        # Fit models\\n        model_A = Ridge(alpha=1.0, random_state=42)\\n        model_B = Ridge(alpha=1.0, random_state=42)\\n        \\n        model_A.fit(X_A_boot, y_boot)\\n        model_B.fit(X_B_boot, y_boot)\\n        \\n        # MSE on OOB\\n        mse_A = mean_squared_error(y_oob, model_A.predict(X_A_oob))\\n        mse_B = mean_squared_error(y_oob, model_B.predict(X_B_oob))\\n        \\n        mse_differences.append(mse_A - mse_B)  # Positive = combined model better\\n    \\n    mse_differences = np.array(mse_differences)\\n    \\n    # One-sided p-value (H1: B reduces MSE compared to A)\\n    p_value = np.mean(mse_differences <= 0)\\n    \\n    # Two-sided p-value also reported\\n    p_value_two_sided = 2 * min(p_value, 1 - p_value)\\n    \\n    # 95% CI for MSE difference\\n    ci_lower = np.percentile(mse_differences, 2.5)\\n    ci_upper = np.percentile(mse_differences, 97.5)\\n    \\n    # MSE reduction percentage\\n    mse_baseline = np.mean([mean_squared_error(y, np.full_like(y, np.mean(y)))])\\n    mean_mse_reduction = np.mean(mse_differences)\\n    mse_reduction_pct = (mean_mse_reduction / mse_baseline) * 100\\n    \\n    return {\\n        'p_value_one_sided': p_value,\\n        'p_value_two_sided': p_value_two_sided,\\n        'mse_differences': mse_differences.tolist(),\\n        'ci_95_lower': ci_lower,\\n        'ci_95_upper': ci_upper,\\n        'mean_mse_reduction': mean_mse_reduction,\\n        'mse_reduction_pct': mse_reduction_pct,\\n        'n_valid_bootstrap': len(mse_differences)\\n    }\\n\\n# Run on both datasets\\nresults_weebit = paired_bootstrap_mse_test(X[sources == 'WeeBIT'], y[sources == 'WeeBIT'], 10000)\\nresults_cefr = paired_bootstrap_mse_test(X[sources == 'CEFR-SP'], y[sources == 'CEFR-SP'], 10000)\\n\\nprint(f\\\"WeeBIT: MSE reduction = {results_weebit['mse_reduction_pct']:.2f}%, p = {results_weebit['p_value_one_sided']:.4f}\\\")\\nprint(f\\\"CEFR-SP: MSE reduction = {results_cefr['mse_reduction_pct']:.2f}%, p = {results_cefr['p_value_one_sided']:.4f}\\\")\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 2: Bootstrap CI for Ridge Regression Coefficients\\n\\n```python\\ndef bootstrap_coefficient_ci(X, y, n_bootstrap=10000, alpha=0.05, random_state=42):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Bootstrap confidence intervals for model coefficients.\\n    \\n    Approach:\\n    1. For each bootstrap sample, fit Ridge regression\\n    2. Store coefficients\\n    3. Compute percentile CI (default 95%)\\n    4. Check if CI excludes 0 (statistical significance)\\n    \\n    Also computes bootstrap standard error and z-statistic p-value.\\n    \\n    Returns: DataFrame with feature, coef, bootstrap_se, ci_lower, ci_upper, p_value, significant\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    np.random.seed(random_state)\\n    n = len(y)\\n    feature_names = X.columns.tolist()\\n    n_features = len(feature_names)\\n    \\n    coef_matrix = np.zeros((n_bootstrap, n_features))\\n    intercept_vector = np.zeros(n_bootstrap)\\n    \\n    for b in range(n_bootstrap):\\n        boot_idx = np.random.choice(n, size=n, replace=True)\\n        \\n        scaler = StandardScaler()\\n        X_boot = scaler.fit_transform(X.iloc[boot_idx])\\n        y_boot = y[boot_idx]\\n        \\n        model = Ridge(alpha=1.0, random_state=42)\\n        model.fit(X_boot, y_boot)\\n        \\n        coef_matrix[b, :] = model.coef_\\n        intercept_vector[b] = model.intercept_\\n    \\n    # Compute statistics\\n    results = []\\n    for i, feature in enumerate(feature_names):\\n        coefs = coef_matrix[:, i]\\n        mean_coef = np.mean(coefs)\\n        bootstrap_se = np.std(coefs)\\n        \\n        # Percentile CI\\n        lower = np.percentile(coefs, (alpha/2) * 100)\\n        upper = np.percentile(coefs, (1 - alpha/2) * 100)\\n        \\n        # P-value: proportion of bootstrap samples where coefficient sign differs from mean\\n        if mean_coef >= 0:\\n            p_val = 2 * np.mean(coefs <= 0)\\n        else:\\n            p_val = 2 * np.mean(coefs >= 0)\\n        \\n        # Significance: CI does not include 0\\n        significant = (lower > 0) if mean_coef > 0 else (upper < 0)\\n        \\n        results.append({\\n            'feature': feature,\\n            'mean_coefficient': mean_coef,\\n            'bootstrap_se': bootstrap_se,\\n            'ci_95_lower': lower,\\n            'ci_95_upper': upper,\\n            'p_value': p_val,\\n            'significant': significant\\n        })\\n    \\n    return pd.DataFrame(results)\\n\\n# Run on combined features model\\nX_combined = X[['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length',\\n                'cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency']]\\n\\ncoef_ci_weebit = bootstrap_coefficient_ci(X_combined[sources == 'WeeBIT'], y[sources == 'WeeBIT'], 10000)\\ncoef_ci_cefr = bootstrap_coefficient_ci(X_combined[sources == 'CEFR-SP'], y[sources == 'CEFR-SP'], 10000)\\n\\nprint(\\\"WeeBIT coefficient significance:\\\")\\nprint(coef_ci_weebit[coef_ci_weebit['significant']][['feature', 'mean_coefficient', 'ci_95_lower', 'ci_95_upper']])\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 3: Proper Cross-Validation with Train/Test Separation\\n\\n```python\\ndef cross_val_evaluation(X, y, model_type='Ridge', n_splits=5, random_state=42):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Proper cross-validation with clear train/test separation.\\n    **Only test set metrics are reported** (training metrics are NOT reported\\n    to avoid optimistic bias).\\n    \\n    Uses sklearn KFold with shuffle=True.\\n    \\n    Returns: dict with test set metrics (mean, SD, per-fold values)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    kf = KFold(n_splits=n_splits, shuffle=True, random_state=random_state)\\n    \\n    test_mse_folds = []\\n    test_r2_folds = []\\n    test_mae_folds = []\\n    all_predictions = []\\n    all_actuals = []\\n    \\n    for fold, (train_idx, test_idx) in enumerate(kf.split(X)):\\n        X_train, X_test = X.iloc[train_idx], X.iloc[test_idx]\\n        y_train, y_test = y[train_idx], y[test_idx]\\n        \\n        # Scale on training, apply to test\\n        scaler = StandardScaler()\\n        X_train_scaled = scaler.fit_transform(X_train)\\n        X_test_scaled = scaler.transform(X_test)\\n        \\n        # Fit on training\\n        if model_type == 'Ridge':\\n            model = Ridge(alpha=1.0, random_state=42)\\n        else:\\n            model = LinearRegression()\\n        \\n        model.fit(X_train_scaled, y_train)\\n        \\n        # Predict test (NO refitting on test!)\\n        y_pred = model.predict(X_test_scaled)\\n        \\n        # Test metrics only\\n        test_mse_folds.append(mean_squared_error(y_test, y_pred))\\n        test_r2_folds.append(r2_score(y_test, y_pred))\\n        test_mae_folds.append(np.mean(np.abs(y_test - y_pred)))\\n        \\n        all_predictions.extend(y_pred.tolist())\\n        all_actuals.extend(y_test.tolist())\\n        \\n        print(f\\\"  Fold {fold+1}: Test R\u00b2 = {test_r2_folds[-1]:.4f}, Test MSE = {test_mse_folds[-1]:.4f}\\\")\\n    \\n    return {\\n        'test_mse_mean': np.mean(test_mse_folds),\\n        'test_mse_sd': np.std(test_mse_folds),\\n        'test_mse_folds': test_mse_folds,\\n        'test_r2_mean': np.mean(test_r2_folds),\\n        'test_r2_sd': np.std(test_r2_folds),\\n        'test_r2_folds': test_r2_folds,\\n        'test_mae_mean': np.mean(test_mae_folds),\\n        'test_mae_sd': np.std(test_mae_folds),\\n        'test_predictions': all_predictions,\\n        'test_actuals': all_actuals\\n    }\\n\\n# Evaluate three model variants\\nmodels_to_evaluate = {\\n    'average_only': ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length'],\\n    'uniformity_only': ['cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency'],\\n    'combined': ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length',\\n                 'cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency']\\n}\\n\\ncv_results = {}\\nfor model_name, features in models_to_evaluate.items():\\n    print(f\\\"\\\\nEvaluating: {model_name}\\\")\\n    cv_results[model_name] = cross_val_evaluation(X[features], y, 'Ridge', 5)\\n    \\n# Print comparison table\\nprint(\\\"\\\\n\\\" + \\\"=\\\"*60)\\nprint(\\\"CROSS-VALIDATED TEST SET PERFORMANCE (mean \u00b1 SD)\\\")\\nprint(\\\"=\\\"*60)\\nfor model_name in ['average_only', 'uniformity_only', 'combined']:\\n    r = cv_results[model_name]\\n    print(f\\\"{model_name:20s}: R\u00b2 = {r['test_r2_mean']:.4f} \u00b1 {r['test_r2_sd']:.4f}, \\\"\\n          f\\\"MSE = {r['test_mse_mean']:.4f} \u00b1 {r['test_mse_sd']:.4f}\\\")\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 4: Effect Size Analysis\\n\\n```python\\ndef compute_effect_sizes(cv_results, n):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute effect sizes for R\u00b2 improvements.\\n    \\n    Approach 1: R\u00b2 difference as effect size (simple, interpretable)\\n    - Report: mean R\u00b2 difference, 95% bootstrap CI for difference\\n    \\n    Approach 2: Cohen's d for R\u00b2 improvement\\n    - Convert R\u00b2 to correlation: r = sqrt(R\u00b2)\\n    - Compute Cohen's d for the correlation difference\\n    - Interpretation: d = 0.2 (small), 0.5 (medium), 0.8 (large)\\n    \\n    Approach 3: Practical significance via R\u00b2 classification (Cohen, 1988)\\n    - R\u00b2 = 0.01 (small), 0.09 (medium), 0.25 (large)\\n    \\n    Returns: dict with effect size measures\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    r2_avg = np.array(cv_results['average_only']['test_r2_folds'])\\n    r2_combined = np.array(cv_results['combined']['test_r2_folds'])\\n    \\n    # R\u00b2 difference\\n    r2_diff = r2_combined - r2_avg\\n    mean_diff = np.mean(r2_diff)\\n    sd_diff = np.std(r2_diff)\\n    \\n    # Bootstrap CI for R\u00b2 difference\\n    n_folds = len(r2_diff)\\n    r2_diff_boot = []\\n    for b in range(10000):\\n        idx = np.random.choice(n_folds, n_folds, replace=True)\\n        r2_diff_boot.append(np.mean(r2_combined[idx] - r2_avg[idx]))\\n    ci_lower = np.percentile(r2_diff_boot, 2.5)\\n    ci_upper = np.percentile(r2_diff_boot, 97.5)\\n    \\n    # Cohen's d for R\u00b2 improvement (using correlation conversion)\\n    # Convert R\u00b2 to correlation, then compute d from correlation\\n    r_avg = np.sqrt(np.maximum(r2_avg, 0))  # Avoid negative R\u00b2\\n    r_combined = np.sqrt(np.maximum(r2_combined, 0))\\n    \\n    # Cohen's d from correlation: d = 2r / sqrt(1 - r^2)\\n    # Compute for each fold, then average\\n    d_values = []\\n    for r_a, r_c in zip(r_avg, r_combined):\\n        if r_a < 1 and r_c < 1:\\n            d_a = 2 * r_a / np.sqrt(1 - r_a**2 + 1e-10)\\n            d_c = 2 * r_c / np.sqrt(1 - r_c**2 + 1e-10)\\n            d_values.append(d_c - d_a)  # Difference in d\\n    \\n    cohens_d = np.mean(d_values) if d_values else 0.0\\n    \\n    # Interpretation\\n    abs_d = abs(cohens_d)\\n    if abs_d < 0.2:\\n        interpretation = 'negligible'\\n    elif abs_d < 0.5:\\n        interpretation = 'small'\\n    elif abs_d < 0.8:\\n        interpretation = 'medium'\\n    else:\\n        interpretation = 'large'\\n    \\n    # Percentage variance explained gained\\n    pct_improvement = (mean_diff / np.mean(r2_avg)) * 100 if np.mean(r2_avg) > 0 else 0\\n    \\n    return {\\n        'r2_difference_mean': mean_diff,\\n        'r2_difference_sd': sd_diff,\\n        'r2_difference_ci_95': (ci_lower, ci_upper),\\n        'cohens_d': cohens_d,\\n        'cohens_d_interpretation': interpretation,\\n        'mse_reduction_pct': (1 - np.mean(r2_combined) / np.mean(r2_avg)) * 100,  # Approximate\\n        'practical_significance': 'large' if mean_diff > 0.05 else ('medium' if mean_diff > 0.02 else 'small')\\n    }\\n\\neffect_sizes_weebit = compute_effect_sizes(\\n    {k: {fold: cv_results[k]['test_r2_folds'][i] for i in range(5)} for k in cv_results},\\n    len(y[sources == 'WeeBIT'])\\n)\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 5: Ablation Study\\n\\n```python\\ndef ablation_study(X, y, n_splits=5):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Ablation study: test each uniformity feature individually.\\n    \\n    Design:\\n    (A) Add-one-in: Start with average features, add one uniformity feature at a time\\n    (B) Remove-one-out: Start with combined features, remove one uniformity feature at a time\\n    \\n    Returns: DataFrame with R\u00b2 for each ablation condition\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    avg_features = ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length']\\n    uniformity_features = ['cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency']\\n    \\n    results = []\\n    \\n    # Baseline: average only\\n    baseline = cross_val_evaluation(X[avg_features], y, 'Ridge', n_splits)\\n    results.append({\\n        'condition': 'average_only (baseline)',\\n        'features_used': avg_features,\\n        'test_r2_mean': baseline['test_r2_mean'],\\n        'test_r2_sd': baseline['test_r2_sd'],\\n        'r2_above_baseline': 0.0\\n    })\\n    \\n    # Add-one-in ablation\\n    for uf in uniformity_features:\\n        features = avg_features + [uf]\\n        result = cross_val_evaluation(X[features], y, 'Ridge', n_splits)\\n        results.append({\\n            'condition': f'average + {uf}',\\n            'features_used': features,\\n            'test_r2_mean': result['test_r2_mean'],\\n            'test_r2_sd': result['test_r2_sd'],\\n            'r2_above_baseline': result['test_r2_mean'] - baseline['test_r2_mean']\\n        })\\n    \\n    # Full combined\\n    combined_features = avg_features + uniformity_features\\n    combined_result = cross_val_evaluation(X[combined_features], y, 'Ridge', n_splits)\\n    results.append({\\n        'condition': 'combined (all features)',\\n        'features_used': combined_features,\\n        'test_r2_mean': combined_result['test_r2_mean'],\\n        'test_r2_sd': combined_result['test_r2_sd'],\\n        'r2_above_baseline': combined_result['test_r2_mean'] - baseline['test_r2_mean']\\n    })\\n    \\n    # Remove-one-out ablation\\n    for uf in uniformity_features:\\n        features = [f for f in combined_features if f != uf]\\n        result = cross_val_evaluation(X[features], y, 'Ridge', n_splits)\\n        results.append({\\n            'condition': f'combined without {uf}',\\n            'features_used': features,\\n            'test_r2_mean': result['test_r2_mean'],\\n            'test_r2_sd': result['test_r2_sd'],\\n            'r2_drop': combined_result['test_r2_mean'] - result['test_r2_mean']\\n        })\\n    \\n    return pd.DataFrame(results)\\n\\nablation_weebit = ablation_study(X[sources == 'WeeBIT'], y[sources == 'WeeBIT'])\\nablation_cefr = ablation_study(X[sources == 'CEFR-SP'], y[sources == 'CEFR-SP'])\\n\\nprint(\\\"\\\\n\\\" + \\\"=\\\"*60)\\nprint(\\\"ABLATION STUDY RESULTS\\\")\\nprint(\\\"=\\\"*60)\\nprint(ablation_weebit[['condition', 'test_r2_mean', 'r2_above_baseline']].to_string())\\n```\\n\\n## Output Generation: Publication-Ready Tables\\n\\n```python\\ndef generate_method_out(results_dict):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Generate method_out.json with all statistical results.\\n    \\n    Output structure:\\n    {\\n        'experiment_info': {...},\\n        'dataset_summary': {...},\\n        'model_performance': {...},  # Table 1\\n        'bootstrap_mse_test': {...},  # Table 2\\n        'coefficient_ci': {...},  # Table 3\\n        'effect_sizes': {...},  # Table 4\\n        'ablation_results': {...},  # Table 5\\n        'all_results_json_serializable': True\\n    }\\n    \\n    All numpy arrays and DataFrames are converted to lists/dicts for JSON serialization.\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    output = {\\n    },\\n        'model_performance': {\\n            'weebit': {\\n                'average_only': format_cv_results(cv_results['average_only']),\\n                'uniformity_only':         'cefr_sp': effect_sizes_cefr\\n        },\\n        'ablation_results': {\\n            'weebit': ablation_weebit.to_dict('records'),\\n            'cefr_sp': ablation_cefr.to_dict('records')\\n        }\\n    }\\n    \\n    # Remove non-serializable items (large arrays)\\n    # Keep only summary statistics, not full bootstrap distributions\\n    \\n \\\"\\\"\\\"Format CV results for JSON output (exclude predictions).\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    return {\\n        'test_r2_mean': float(cv_dict['test_r2_mean']),\\n        'test_r2_sd': float(cv_dict['test_r2_sd']),\\n        'test_r2_folds': [float(x) for x in cv_dict['test_r2_folds']],\\n        'test_mse_mean': float(cv_dict['test_mse_mean']),\\n        'test_mse_sd': float(cv_dict['test_mse_sd']),\\n        'test_mse_folds': [float(x) for x in cv_dict['test_mse_folds']],\\n        'test_mae_mean': float(cv_dict['test_mae_mean']),\\n        'test_mae_sd': float(cv_dict['test_mae_sd'])\\n    }\\n\\n# Generate output\\ngenerate_method_out(all_results)\\n```\\n\\n## Execution Timeline (6 hours budget)\\n\\n```\\nHour 0-1: Setup and feature computation\\n-   "new_str": "{\n  \"title\": \"Statistical evaluation of uniformity features for readability\",\n  \"summary\": \"Comprehensive statistical evaluation of the Uniformity Principle hypothesis: bootstrap significance tests for MSE reduction, feature coefficient uncertainty quantification, proper train/test reporting, effect size analysis (Cohen's d), and ablation studies to identify which uniformity features contribute uniquely to readability prediction.\",\n  \"runpod_compute_profile\": \"cpu_light\",\n  \"implementation_pseudocode\": \"## Overview\\n\\nThis experiment conducts comprehensive statistical evaluation of the Uniformity Principle hypothesis using the WeeBIT and CEFR-SP datasets (13,129 sentences total). The evaluation addresses five key statistical requirements: (1) paired bootstrap test for MSE reduction significance, (2) bootstrap CI for feature coefficients, (3) proper train/test reporting, (4) effect size analysis, and (5) ablation studies.\\n\\n**Key Statistical Approaches**:\\n- Bootstrap hypothesis testing (10,000 samples) for MSE reduction significance\\n- Bootstrap percentile confidence intervals for Ridge regression coefficients\\n- 5-fold cross-validation with proper train/test separation (reporting test metrics only)\\n- Effect size: R\u00b2 improvement with 95% CI, and Cohen's d for practical significance\\n- Ablation: add-one-in and remove-one-out uniformity feature analysis\\n\\n## Data Loading and Feature Computation\\n\\n```python\\nimport json\\nimport numpy as np\\nimport pandas as pd\\nfrom sklearn.model_selection import KFold\\nfrom sklearn.linear_model import Ridge\\nfrom sklearn.metrics import mean_squared_error, r2_score\\nfrom sklearn.preprocessing import StandardScaler\\nimport scipy.stats as stats\\nimport pronouncing  # For CMUdict syllable counting\\n\\n# Load datasets from dependency artifact\\ndef load_datasets():\\n    with open('full_data_out.json', 'r') as f:\\n        data = json.load(f)\\n    \\n    sentences = []\\n    scores = []\\n    sources = []\\n    \\n    for dataset in data['datasets']:\\n        for example in dataset['examples']:\\n            sentences.append(example['input'])\\n            scores.append(float(example['output']))\\n            sources.append(dataset['dataset'])\\n    \\n    return sentences, np.array(scores), np.array(sources)\\n\\nsentences, y, sources = load_datasets()\\nprint(f\\\"Loaded {len(sentences)} sentences\\\")\\nprint(f\\\"WeeBIT: {np.sum(sources == 'WeeBIT')}, CEFR-SP: {np.sum(sources == 'CEFR-SP')}\\\")\\n\\ndef syllable_count(word):\\n    word = word.lower().strip('.,!?;:')\\n    phones = pronouncing.phones_for_word(word)\\n    if phones:\\n        return pronouncing.syllable_count(phones[0])\\n    else:\\n        vowels = 'aeiouy'\\n        count = 0\\n        prev_was_vowel = False\\n        for char in word:\\n            is_vowel = char in vowels\\n            if is_vowel and not prev_was_vowel:\\n                count += 1\\n            prev_was_vowel = is_vowel\\n        if word.endswith('e'):\\n            count = max(1, count - 1)\\n        return max(1, count)\\n\\ndef get_word_frequency(word):\\n    # Implementation: load SUBTLEX-US data or use NLTK frequencies\\n    # Return log frequency (higher = more frequent = easier)\\n    pass\\n\\ndef extract_features(sentences):\\n    features_list = []\\n    for sent in sentences:\\n        words = [w for w in sent.split() if w]\\n        if len(words) == 0:\\n            features_list.append({'avg_word_length': 0.0, 'avg_syllables': 0.0, 'avg_frequency': 0.0,\\n                                  'cv_word_length': 0.0, 'cv_syllables': 0.0, 'cv_frequency': 0.0,\\n                                  'sentence_length': 0.0})\\n            continue\\n        \\n        word_lengths = np.array([len(w) for w in words])\\n        avg_wl = np.mean(word_lengths)\\n        cv_wl = np.std(word_lengths) / (avg_wl + 1e-10)\\n        \\n        syll_counts = np.array([syllable_count(w) for w in words])\\n        avg_syll = np.mean(syll_counts)\\n        cv_syll = np.std(syll_counts) / (avg_syll + 1e-10)\\n        \\n        freqs = np.array([get_word_frequency(w) for w in words])\\n        avg_freq = np.mean(freqs)\\n        cv_freq = np.std(freqs) / (avg_freq + 1e-10)\\n        \\n        features_list.append({\\n            'avg_word_length': avg_wl,\\n            'avg_syllables': avg_syll,\\n            'avg_frequency': avg_freq,\\n            'cv_word_length': cv_wl,\\n            'cv_syllables': cv_syll,\\n            'cv_frequency': cv_freq,\\n            'sentence_length': len(words)\\n        })\\n    \\n    return pd.DataFrame(features_list)\\n\\nX = extract_features(sentences)\\nprint(f\\\"Features shape: {X.shape}\\\")\\nprint(f\\\"Any NaN? {X.isnull().any().any()}\\\")\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 1: Paired Bootstrap Test for MSE Reduction Significance\\n\\n```python\\ndef paired_bootstrap_mse_test(X, y, n_bootstrap=10000, random_state=42):\\n    np.random.seed(random_state)\\n    n = len(y)\\n    \\n    avg_features = ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length']\\n    uniformity_features = ['cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency']\\n    combined_features = avg_features + uniformity_features\\n    \\n    mse_differences = []\\n    \\n    for b in range(n_bootstrap):\\n        boot_idx = np.random.choice(n, size=n, replace=True)\\n        oob_idx = np.setdiff1d(np.arange(n), boot_idx)\\n        \\n        if len(oob_idx) < 10:\\n            continue\\n        \\n        scaler_A = StandardScaler()\\n        scaler_B = StandardScaler()\\n        \\n        X_A_boot = scaler_A.fit_transform(X.loc[boot_idx, avg_features])\\n        X_A_oob = scaler_A.transform(X.loc[oob_idx, avg_features])\\n        \\n        X_B_boot = scaler_B.fit_transform(X.loc[boot_idx, combined_features])\\n        X_B_oob = scaler_B.transform(X.loc[oob_idx, combined_features])\\n        \\n        y_boot = y[boot_idx]\\n        y_oob = y[oob_idx]\\n        \\n        model_A = Ridge(alpha=1.0, random_state=42)\\n        model_B = Ridge(alpha=1.0, random_state=42)\\n        \\n        model_A.fit(X_A_boot, y_boot)\\n        model_B.fit(X_B_boot, y_boot)\\n        \\n        mse_A = mean_squared_error(y_oob, model_A.predict(X_A_oob))\\n        mse_B = mean_squared_error(y_oob, model_B.predict(X_B_oob))\\n        \\n        mse_differences.append(mse_A - mse_B)\\n    \\n    mse_differences = np.array(mse_differences)\\n    \\n    p_value = np.mean(mse_differences <= 0)\\n    \\n    ci_lower = np.percentile(mse_differences, 2.5)\\n    ci_upper = np.percentile(mse_differences, 97.5)\\n    \\n    mse_baseline = np.mean([mean_squared_error(y, np.full_like(y, np.mean(y)))])\\n    mean_mse_reduction = np.mean(mse_differences)\\n    mse_reduction_pct = (mean_mse_reduction / mse_baseline) * 100\\n    \\n    return {\\n        'p_value_one_sided': p_value,\\n        'p_value_two_sided': 2 * min(p_value, 1 - p_value),\\n        'ci_95_lower': ci_lower,\\n        'ci_95_upper': ci_upper,\\n        'mean_mse_reduction': mean_mse_reduction,\\n        'mse_reduction_pct': mse_reduction_pct,\\n        'n_valid_bootstrap': len(mse_differences)\\n    }\\n\\nresults_weebit = paired_bootstrap_mse_test(X[sources == 'WeeBIT'], y[sources == 'WeeBIT'], 10000)\\nresults_cefr = paired_bootstrap_mse_test(X[sources == 'CEFR-SP'], y[sources == 'CEFR-SP'], 10000)\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 2: Bootstrap CI for Ridge Regression Coefficients\\n\\n```python\\ndef bootstrap_coefficient_ci(X, y, n_bootstrap=10000, alpha=0.05, random_state=42):\\n    np.random.seed(random_state)\\n    n = len(y)\\n    feature_names = X.columns.tolist()\\n    n_features = len(feature_names)\\n    \\n    coef_matrix = np.zeros((n_bootstrap, n_features))\\n    \\n    for b in range(n_bootstrap):\\n        boot_idx = np.random.choice(n, size=n, replace=True)\\n        \\n        scaler = StandardScaler()\\n        X_boot = scaler.fit_transform(X.iloc[boot_idx])\\n        y_boot = y[boot_idx]\\n        \\n        model = Ridge(alpha=1.0, random_state=42)\\n        model.fit(X_boot, y_boot)\\n        \\n        coef_matrix[b, :] = model.coef_\\n    \\n    results = []\\n    for i, feature in enumerate(feature_names):\\n        coefs = coef_matrix[:, i]\\n        mean_coef = np.mean(coefs)\\n        bootstrap_se = np.std(coefs)\\n        \\n        lower = np.percentile(coefs, (alpha/2) * 100)\\n        upper = np.percentile(coefs, (1 - alpha/2) * 100)\\n        \\n        if mean_coef >= 0:\\n            p_val = 2 * np.mean(coefs <= 0)\\n        else:\\n            p_val = 2 * np.mean(coefs >= 0)\\n        \\n        significant = (lower > 0) if mean_coef > 0 else (upper < 0)\\n        \\n        results.append({\\n            'feature': feature,\\n            'mean_coefficient': mean_coef,\\n            'bootstrap_se': bootstrap_se,\\n            'ci_95_lower': lower,\\n            'ci_95_upper': upper,\\n            'p_value': p_val,\\n            'significant': significant\\n        })\\n    \\n    return pd.DataFrame(results)\\n\\nX_combined = X[['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length',\\n                'cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency']]\\n\\ncoef_ci_weebit = bootstrap_coefficient_ci(X_combined[sources == 'WeeBIT'], y[sources == 'WeeBIT'], 10000)\\ncoef_ci_cefr = bootstrap_coefficient_ci(X_combined[sources == 'CEFR-SP'], y[sources == 'CEFR-SP'], 10000)\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 3: Proper Cross-Validation with Train/Test Separation\\n\\n```python\\ndef cross_val_evaluation(X, y, model_type='Ridge', n_splits=5, random_state=42):\\n    kf = KFold(n_splits=n_splits, shuffle=True, random_state=random_state)\\n    \\n    test_mse_folds = []\\n    test_r2_folds = []\\n    test_mae_folds = []\\n    all_predictions = []\\n    all_actuals = []\\n    \\n    for fold, (train_idx, test_idx) in enumerate(kf.split(X)):\\n        X_train, X_test = X.iloc[train_idx], X.iloc[test_idx]\\n        y_train, y_test = y[train_idx], y[test_idx]\\n        \\n        scaler = StandardScaler()\\n        X_train_scaled = scaler.fit_transform(X_train)\\n        X_test_scaled = scaler.transform(X_test)\\n        \\n        if model_type == 'Ridge':\\n            model = Ridge(alpha=1.0, random_state=42)\\n        else:\\n            model = LinearRegression()\\n        \\n        model.fit(X_train_scaled, y_train)\\n        \\n        y_pred = model.predict(X_test_scaled)\\n        \\n        test_mse_folds.append(mean_squared_error(y_test, y_pred))\\n        test_r2_folds.append(r2_score(y_test, y_pred))\\n        test_mae_folds.append(np.mean(np.abs(y_test - y_pred)))\\n        \\n        all_predictions.extend(y_pred.tolist())\\n        all_actuals.extend(y_test.tolist())\\n    \\n    return {\\n        'test_mse_mean': np.mean(test_mse_folds),\\n        'test_mse_sd': np.std(test_mse_folds),\\n        'test_mse_folds': test_mse_folds,\\n        'test_r2_mean': np.mean(test_r2_folds),\\n        'test_r2_sd': np.std(test_r2_folds),\\n        'test_r2_folds': test_r2_folds,\\n        'test_mae_mean': np.mean(test_mae_folds),\\n        'test_mae_sd': np.std(test_mae_folds),\\n        'test_predictions': all_predictions,\\n        'test_actuals': all_actuals\\n    }\\n\\nmodels_to_evaluate = {\\n    'average_only': ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length'],\\n    'uniformity_only': ['cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency'],\\n    'combined': ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length',\\n                 'cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency']\\n}\\n\\ncv_results = {}\\nfor model_name, features in models_to_evaluate.items():\\n    print(f\\\"Evaluating: {model_name}\\\")\\n    cv_results[model_name] = cross_val_evaluation(X[features], y, 'Ridge', 5)\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 4: Effect Size Analysis\\n\\n```python\\ndef compute_effect_sizes(cv_results, n):\\n    r2_avg = np.array(cv_results['average_only']['test_r2_folds'])\\n    r2_combined = np.array(cv_results['combined']['test_r2_folds'])\\n    \\n    r2_diff = r2_combined - r2_avg\\n    mean_diff = np.mean(r2_diff)\\n    sd_diff = np.std(r2_diff)\\n    \\n    n_folds = len(r2_diff)\\n    r2_diff_boot = []\\n    for b in range(10000):\\n        idx = np.random.choice(n_folds, n_folds, replace=True)\\n        r2_diff_boot.append(np.mean(r2_combined[idx] - r2_avg[idx]))\\n    ci_lower = np.percentile(r2_diff_boot, 2.5)\\n    ci_upper = np.percentile(r2_diff_boot, 97.5)\\n    \\n    r_avg = np.sqrt(np.maximum(r2_avg, 0))\\n    r_combined = np.sqrt(np.maximum(r2_combined, 0))\\n    \\n    d_values = []\\n    for r_a, r_c in zip(r_avg, r_combined):\\n        if r_a < 1 and r_c < 1:\\n            d_a = 2 * r_a / np.sqrt(1 - r_a**2 + 1e-10)\\n            d_c = 2 * r_c / np.sqrt(1 - r_c**2 + 1e-10)\\n            d_values.append(d_c - d_a)\\n    \\n    cohens_d = np.mean(d_values) if d_values else 0.0\\n    \\n    abs_d = abs(cohens_d)\\n    if abs_d < 0.2:\\n        interpretation = 'negligible'\\n    elif abs_d < 0.5:\\n        interpretation = 'small'\\n    elif abs_d < 0.8:\\n        interpretation = 'medium'\\n    else:\\n        interpretation = 'large'\\n    \\n    return {\\n        'r2_difference_mean': mean_diff,\\n        'r2_difference_sd': sd_diff,\\n        'r2_difference_ci_95': (ci_lower, ci_upper),\\n        'cohens_d': cohens_d,\\n        'cohens_d_interpretation': interpretation,\\n        'practical_significance': 'large' if mean_diff > 0.05 else ('medium' if mean_diff > 0.02 else 'small')\\n    }\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 5: Ablation Study\\n\\n```python\\ndef ablation_study(X, y, n_splits=5):\\n    avg_features = ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length']\\n    uniformity_features = ['cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency']\\n    \\n    results = []\\n    \\n    baseline 'test_r2_sd': baseline['test_r2_sd'],\\n        'r2_above_baseline': 0.0\\n    })\\n    \\n    for uf in uniformity_features:\\n        features = avg_features + [uf]\\n        result = cross_val_evaluation(X[features], y, 'Ridge', n_splits)\\n        results.append({\\n            'condition': f'average + {uf}',\\n            'test_r2_mean': result['test_r2_mean'],\\n            'test_r2_sd': result['test_r2_sd'],\\n            'r2_above_baseline': result['test_r2_mean'] - baseline['test_r2_mean']\\n        })\\n    \\n    combined_features = avg_features + uniformity_features\\n    combined_result = cross_val_evaluation(X[combined_features], y, 'Ridge', n_splits)\\n    results.append({\\n        'condition': 'combined (all features)',\\n        'test_r2_mean': combined_result['test_r2_mean'],\\n        'test_r2_sd': combined_result['test_r2_sd'],\\n        'r2_above_baseline': combined_result['test_r2_mean'] - baseline['test_r2_mean']\\n    })\\n    \\n    for uf in uniformity_features:\\n        features = [f for f in combined_features if f != uf]\\n        result = cross_val_evaluation(X[features], y, 'Ridge', n_splits)\\n        results.append({\\n            'condition': f'combined without {uf}',\\n            'test_r2_mean': result['test_r2_mean'],\\n            'test_r2_sd': result['test_r2_sd'],\\n            'r2_drop': combined_result['test_r2_mean'] - result['test_r2_mean']\\n        })\\n    \\n    return pd.DataFrame(results)\\n\\nablation_weebit = ablation_study(X[sources == 'WeeBIT'], y[sources == Plan\\n\\nIf the primary approach encounters issues, the following fallback strategies are available:\\n\\n### Issue 1: Bootstrap Computation Too Slow (10,000 samples \u00d7 13,129 {"content": [{"cache_prompt": false, "type": "text", "text": "No replacement was performed, old_str `{\n  \"title\": \"Statistical evaluation of uniformity features for readability\",\n  \"summary\": \"Comprehensive statistical evaluation of the Uniformity Principle hypothesis: bootstrap significance tests for MSE reduction, feature coefficient uncertainty quantification, proper train/test reporting, effect size analysis (Cohen's d), and ablation studies to identify which uniformity features contribute uniquely to readability prediction.\",\n  \"runpod_compute_profile\": \"cpu_light\",\n  \"implementation_pseudocode\": \"## Overview\\n\\nThis experiment conducts comprehensive statistical evaluation of the Uniformity Principle hypothesis using the WeeBIT and CEFR-SP datasets (13,129 sentences total). The evaluation addresses five key statistical requirements: (1) paired bootstrap test for MSE reduction significance, (2) bootstrap CI for feature coefficients, (3) proper train/test reporting, (4) effect size analysis, and (5) ablation studies.\\n\\n**Key Statistical Approaches**:\\n- Bootstrap hypothesis testing (10,000 samples) for MSE reduction significance\\n- Bootstrap percentile confidence intervals for Ridge regression coefficients\\n- 5-fold cross-validation with proper train/test separation (reporting test metrics only)\\n- Effect size: R\u00b2 improvement with 95% CI, and Cohen's d for practical significance\\n- Ablation: add-one-in and remove-one-out uniformity feature analysis\\n\\n## Data Loading and Feature Computation\\n\\n```python\\nimport json\\nimport numpy as np\\nimport pandas as pd\\nfrom sklearn.model_selection import KFold\\nfrom sklearn.linear_model import Ridge\\nfrom sklearn.metrics import mean_squared_error, r2_score\\nfrom sklearn.preprocessing import StandardScaler\\nimport scipy.stats as stats\\nimport pronouncing  # For CMUdict syllable counting\\n\\n# Load datasets from dependency artifact\\ndef load_datasets():\\n    with open('full_data_out.json', 'r') as f:\\n        data = json.load(f)\\n    \\n    sentences = []\\n    scores = []\\n    sources = []\\n    \\n    for dataset in data['datasets']:\\n        for example in dataset['examples']:\\n            sentences.append(example['input'])\\n            # Convert output to float (readability score, normalized 0-1)\\n            scores.append(float(example['output']))\\n            sources.append(dataset['dataset'])\\n    \\n    return sentences, np.array(scores), np.array(sources)\\n\\nsentences, y, sources = load_datasets()\\nprint(f\\\"Loaded {len(sentences)} sentences\\\")\\nprint(f\\\"WeeBIT: {np.sum(sources == 'WeeBIT')}, CEFR-SP: {np.sum(sources == 'CEFR-SP')}\\\")\\n\\ndef syllable_count(word):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Count syllables using CMUdict, with heuristic fallback.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    word = word.lower().strip('.,!?;:')\\n    phones = pronouncing.phones_for_word(word)\\n    if phones:\\n        return pronouncing.syllable_count(phones[0])\\n    else:\\n        # Heuristic fallback: count vowel groups\\n        vowels = 'aeiouy'\\n        count = 0\\n        prev_was_vowel = False\\n        for char in word:\\n            is_vowel = char in vowels\\n            if is_vowel and not prev_was_vowel:\\n                count += 1\\n            prev_was_vowel = is_vowel\\n        if word.endswith('e'):\\n            count = max(1, count - 1)\\n        return max(1, count)\\n\\ndef get_word_frequency(word):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Get word frequency using SUBTLEX-US norms or NLTK fallback.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Implementation: load SUBTLEX-US data from file or use NLTK frequencies\\n    # Return log frequency (higher = more frequent = easier)\\n    pass  # Detailed implementation in executor\\n\\ndef extract_features(sentences):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute both average and uniformity (CV) features for each sentence.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    features_list = []\\n    for sent in sentences:\\n        words = [w for w in sent.split() if w]  # Remove empty strings\\n        if len(words) == 0:\\n            features_list.append({f: 0.0 for f in ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', \\n                                                      'cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency',\\n                                                      'sentence_length']})\\n            continue\\n        \\n        # Word lengths\\n        word_lengths = np.array([len(w) for w in words])\\n        avg_wl = np.mean(word_lengths)\\n        cv_wl = np.std(word_lengths) / (avg_wl + 1e-10)\\n        \\n        # Syllable counts\\n        syll_counts = np.array([syllable_count(w) for w in words])\\n        avg_syll = np.mean(syll_counts)\\n        cv_syll = np.std(syll_counts) / (avg_syll + 1e-10)\\n        \\n        # Word frequencies\\n        freqs = np.array([get_word_frequency(w) for w in words])\\n        avg_freq = np.mean(freqs)\\n        cv_freq = np.std(freqs) / (avg_freq + 1e-10)\\n        \\n        features_list.append({\\n            'avg_word_length': avg_wl,\\n            'avg_syllables': avg_syll,\\n            'avg_frequency': avg_freq,\\n            'cv_word_length': cv_wl,\\n            'cv_syllables': cv_syll,\\n            'cv_frequency': cv_freq,\\n            'sentence_length': len(words)\\n        })\\n    \\n    return pd.DataFrame(features_list)\\n\\nX = extract_features(sentences)\\nprint(f\\\"Features shape: {X.shape}\\\")\\nprint(f\\\"Any NaN? {X.isnull().any().any()}\\\")\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 1: Paired Bootstrap Test for MSE Reduction Significance\\n\\n```python\\ndef paired_bootstrap_mse_test(X, y, n_bootstrap=10000, random_state=42):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Paired bootstrap test for whether adding uniformity features reduces MSE.\\n    \\n    H0: Adding uniformity features does NOT reduce MSE (MSE_combined >= MSE_average)\\n    H1: Adding uniformity features reduces MSE (MSE_combined < MSE_average)\\n    \\n    Approach (out-of-bag bootstrap):\\n    1. For each bootstrap iteration b:\\n       - Sample n indices with replacement from [0, n-1]\\n       - Fit Model A (average features) and Model B (combined) on bootstrap sample\\n       - Predict on out-of-bag (OOB) samples\\n       - Compute MSE_A and MSE_B on OOB\\n       - Record: mse_diff = MSE_A - MSE_B (positive = B better)\\n    \\n    2. One-sided p-value = proportion of bootstrap samples where mse_diff <= 0\\n       (i.e., proportion where B is NOT better)\\n    \\n    3. 95% CI for MSE difference = [2.5 percentile, 97.5 percentile] of mse_differences\\n    \\n    4. MSE reduction % = (mean(mse_differences) / MSE_baseline) * 100\\n    \\n    Returns: dict with p_value, ci_95, mse_reduction_pct, mse_differences\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    np.random.seed(random_state)\\n    n = len(y)\\n    \\n    avg_features = ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length']\\n    uniformity_features = ['cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency']\\n    combined_features = avg_features + uniformity_features\\n    \\n    mse_differences = []\\n    \\n    for b in range(n_bootstrap):\\n        # Bootstrap sample\\n        boot_idx = np.random.choice(n, size=n, replace=True)\\n        oob_idx = np.setdiff1d(np.arange(n), boot_idx)\\n        \\n        if len(oob_idx) < 10:  # Need at least 10 OOB samples\\n            continue\\n        \\n        # Scale features per bootstrap sample\\n        scaler_A = StandardScaler()\\n        scaler_B = StandardScaler()\\n        \\n        X_A_boot = scaler_A.fit_transform(X.loc[boot_idx, avg_features])\\n        X_A_oob = scaler_A.transform(X.loc[oob_idx, avg_features])\\n        \\n        X_B_boot = scaler_B.fit_transform(X.loc[boot_idx, combined_features])\\n        X_B_oob = scaler_B.transform(X.loc[oob_idx, combined_features])\\n        \\n        y_boot = y[boot_idx]\\n        y_oob = y[oob_idx]\\n        \\n        # Fit models\\n        model_A = Ridge(alpha=1.0, random_state=42)\\n        model_B = Ridge(alpha=1.0, random_state=42)\\n        \\n        model_A.fit(X_A_boot, y_boot)\\n        model_B.fit(X_B_boot, y_boot)\\n        \\n        # MSE on OOB\\n        mse_A = mean_squared_error(y_oob, model_A.predict(X_A_oob))\\n        mse_B = mean_squared_error(y_oob, model_B.predict(X_B_oob))\\n        \\n        mse_differences.append(mse_A - mse_B)  # Positive = combined model better\\n    \\n    mse_differences = np.array(mse_differences)\\n    \\n    # One-sided p-value (H1: B reduces MSE compared to A)\\n    p_value = np.mean(mse_differences <= 0)\\n    \\n    # Two-sided p-value also reported\\n    p_value_two_sided = 2 * min(p_value, 1 - p_value)\\n    \\n    # 95% CI for MSE difference\\n    ci_lower = np.percentile(mse_differences, 2.5)\\n    ci_upper = np.percentile(mse_differences, 97.5)\\n    \\n    # MSE reduction percentage\\n    mse_baseline = np.mean([mean_squared_error(y, np.full_like(y, np.mean(y)))])\\n    mean_mse_reduction = np.mean(mse_differences)\\n    mse_reduction_pct = (mean_mse_reduction / mse_baseline) * 100\\n    \\n    return {\\n        'p_value_one_sided': p_value,\\n        'p_value_two_sided': p_value_two_sided,\\n        'mse_differences': mse_differences.tolist(),\\n        'ci_95_lower': ci_lower,\\n        'ci_95_upper': ci_upper,\\n        'mean_mse_reduction': mean_mse_reduction,\\n        'mse_reduction_pct': mse_reduction_pct,\\n        'n_valid_bootstrap': len(mse_differences)\\n    }\\n\\n# Run on both datasets\\nresults_weebit = paired_bootstrap_mse_test(X[sources == 'WeeBIT'], y[sources == 'WeeBIT'], 10000)\\nresults_cefr = paired_bootstrap_mse_test(X[sources == 'CEFR-SP'], y[sources == 'CEFR-SP'], 10000)\\n\\nprint(f\\\"WeeBIT: MSE reduction = {results_weebit['mse_reduction_pct']:.2f}%, p = {results_weebit['p_value_one_sided']:.4f}\\\")\\nprint(f\\\"CEFR-SP: MSE reduction = {results_cefr['mse_reduction_pct']:.2f}%, p = {results_cefr['p_value_one_sided']:.4f}\\\")\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 2: Bootstrap CI for Ridge Regression Coefficients\\n\\n```python\\ndef bootstrap_coefficient_ci(X, y, n_bootstrap=10000, alpha=0.05, random_state=42):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Bootstrap confidence intervals for model coefficients.\\n    \\n    Approach:\\n    1. For each bootstrap sample, fit Ridge regression\\n    2. Store coefficients\\n    3. Compute percentile CI (default 95%)\\n    4. Check if CI excludes 0 (statistical significance)\\n    \\n    Also computes bootstrap standard error and z-statistic p-value.\\n    \\n    Returns: DataFrame with feature, coef, bootstrap_se, ci_lower, ci_upper, p_value, significant\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    np.random.seed(random_state)\\n    n = len(y)\\n    feature_names = X.columns.tolist()\\n    n_features = len(feature_names)\\n    \\n    coef_matrix = np.zeros((n_bootstrap, n_features))\\n    intercept_vector = np.zeros(n_bootstrap)\\n    \\n    for b in range(n_bootstrap):\\n        boot_idx = np.random.choice(n, size=n, replace=True)\\n        \\n        scaler = StandardScaler()\\n        X_boot = scaler.fit_transform(X.iloc[boot_idx])\\n        y_boot = y[boot_idx]\\n        \\n        model = Ridge(alpha=1.0, random_state=42)\\n        model.fit(X_boot, y_boot)\\n        \\n        coef_matrix[b, :] = model.coef_\\n        intercept_vector[b] = model.intercept_\\n    \\n    # Compute statistics\\n    results = []\\n    for i, feature in enumerate(feature_names):\\n        coefs = coef_matrix[:, i]\\n        mean_coef = np.mean(coefs)\\n        bootstrap_se = np.std(coefs)\\n        \\n        # Percentile CI\\n        lower = np.percentile(coefs, (alpha/2) * 100)\\n        upper = np.percentile(coefs, (1 - alpha/2) * 100)\\n        \\n        # P-value: proportion of bootstrap samples where coefficient sign differs from mean\\n        if mean_coef >= 0:\\n            p_val = 2 * np.mean(coefs <= 0)\\n        else:\\n            p_val = 2 * np.mean(coefs >= 0)\\n        \\n        # Significance: CI does not include 0\\n        significant = (lower > 0) if mean_coef > 0 else (upper < 0)\\n        \\n        results.append({\\n            'feature': feature,\\n            'mean_coefficient': mean_coef,\\n            'bootstrap_se': bootstrap_se,\\n            'ci_95_lower': lower,\\n            'ci_95_upper': upper,\\n            'p_value': p_val,\\n            'significant': significant\\n        })\\n    \\n    return pd.DataFrame(results)\\n\\n# Run on combined features model\\nX_combined = X[['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length',\\n                'cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency']]\\n\\ncoef_ci_weebit = bootstrap_coefficient_ci(X_combined[sources == 'WeeBIT'], y[sources == 'WeeBIT'], 10000)\\ncoef_ci_cefr = bootstrap_coefficient_ci(X_combined[sources == 'CEFR-SP'], y[sources == 'CEFR-SP'], 10000)\\n\\nprint(\\\"WeeBIT coefficient significance:\\\")\\nprint(coef_ci_weebit[coef_ci_weebit['significant']][['feature', 'mean_coefficient', 'ci_95_lower', 'ci_95_upper']])\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 3: Proper Cross-Validation with Train/Test Separation\\n\\n```python\\ndef cross_val_evaluation(X, y, model_type='Ridge', n_splits=5, random_state=42):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Proper cross-validation with clear train/test separation.\\n    **Only test set metrics are reported** (training metrics are NOT reported\\n    to avoid optimistic bias).\\n    \\n    Uses sklearn KFold with shuffle=True.\\n    \\n    Returns: dict with test set metrics (mean, SD, per-fold values)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    kf = KFold(n_splits=n_splits, shuffle=True, random_state=random_state)\\n    \\n    test_mse_folds = []\\n    test_r2_folds = []\\n    test_mae_folds = []\\n    all_predictions = []\\n    all_actuals = []\\n    \\n    for fold, (train_idx, test_idx) in enumerate(kf.split(X)):\\n        X_train, X_test = X.iloc[train_idx], X.iloc[test_idx]\\n        y_train, y_test = y[train_idx], y[test_idx]\\n        \\n        # Scale on training, apply to test\\n        scaler = StandardScaler()\\n        X_train_scaled = scaler.fit_transform(X_train)\\n        X_test_scaled = scaler.transform(X_test)\\n        \\n        # Fit on training\\n        if model_type == 'Ridge':\\n            model = Ridge(alpha=1.0, random_state=42)\\n        else:\\n            model = LinearRegression()\\n        \\n        model.fit(X_train_scaled, y_train)\\n        \\n        # Predict test (NO refitting on test!)\\n        y_pred = model.predict(X_test_scaled)\\n        \\n        # Test metrics only\\n        test_mse_folds.append(mean_squared_error(y_test, y_pred))\\n        test_r2_folds.append(r2_score(y_test, y_pred))\\n        test_mae_folds.append(np.mean(np.abs(y_test - y_pred)))\\n        \\n        all_predictions.extend(y_pred.tolist())\\n        all_actuals.extend(y_test.tolist())\\n        \\n        print(f\\\"  Fold {fold+1}: Test R\u00b2 = {test_r2_folds[-1]:.4f}, Test MSE = {test_mse_folds[-1]:.4f}\\\")\\n    \\n    return {\\n        'test_mse_mean': np.mean(test_mse_folds),\\n        'test_mse_sd': np.std(test_mse_folds),\\n        'test_mse_folds': test_mse_folds,\\n        'test_r2_mean': np.mean(test_r2_folds),\\n        'test_r2_sd': np.std(test_r2_folds),\\n        'test_r2_folds': test_r2_folds,\\n        'test_mae_mean': np.mean(test_mae_folds),\\n        'test_mae_sd': np.std(test_mae_folds),\\n        'test_predictions': all_predictions,\\n        'test_actuals': all_actuals\\n    }\\n\\n# Evaluate three model variants\\nmodels_to_evaluate = {\\n    'average_only': ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length'],\\n    'uniformity_only': ['cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency'],\\n    'combined': ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length',\\n                 'cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency']\\n}\\n\\ncv_results = {}\\nfor model_name, features in models_to_evaluate.items():\\n    print(f\\\"\\\\nEvaluating: {model_name}\\\")\\n    cv_results[model_name] = cross_val_evaluation(X[features], y, 'Ridge', 5)\\n    \\n# Print comparison table\\nprint(\\\"\\\\n\\\" + \\\"=\\\"*60)\\nprint(\\\"CROSS-VALIDATED TEST SET PERFORMANCE (mean \u00b1 SD)\\\")\\nprint(\\\"=\\\"*60)\\nfor model_name in ['average_only', 'uniformity_only', 'combined']:\\n    r = cv_results[model_name]\\n    print(f\\\"{model_name:20s}: R\u00b2 = {r['test_r2_mean']:.4f} \u00b1 {r['test_r2_sd']:.4f}, \\\"\\n          f\\\"MSE = {r['test_mse_mean']:.4f} \u00b1 {r['test_mse_sd']:.4f}\\\")\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 4: Effect Size Analysis\\n\\n```python\\ndef compute_effect_sizes(cv_results, n):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute effect sizes for R\u00b2 improvements.\\n    \\n    Approach 1: R\u00b2 difference as effect size (simple, interpretable)\\n    - Report: mean R\u00b2 difference, 95% bootstrap CI for difference\\n    \\n    Approach 2: Cohen's d for R\u00b2 improvement\\n    - Convert R\u00b2 to correlation: r = sqrt(R\u00b2)\\n    - Compute Cohen's d for the correlation difference\\n    - Interpretation: d = 0.2 (small), 0.5 (medium), 0.8 (large)\\n    \\n    Approach 3: Practical significance via R\u00b2 classification (Cohen, 1988)\\n    - R\u00b2 = 0.01 (small), 0.09 (medium), 0.25 (large)\\n    \\n    Returns: dict with effect size measures\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    r2_avg = np.array(cv_results['average_only']['test_r2_folds'])\\n    r2_combined = np.array(cv_results['combined']['test_r2_folds'])\\n    \\n    # R\u00b2 difference\\n    r2_diff = r2_combined - r2_avg\\n    mean_diff = np.mean(r2_diff)\\n    sd_diff = np.std(r2_diff)\\n    \\n    # Bootstrap CI for R\u00b2 difference\\n    n_folds = len(r2_diff)\\n    r2_diff_boot = []\\n    for b in range(10000):\\n        idx = np.random.choice(n_folds, n_folds, replace=True)\\n        r2_diff_boot.append(np.mean(r2_combined[idx] - r2_avg[idx]))\\n    ci_lower = np.percentile(r2_diff_boot, 2.5)\\n    ci_upper = np.percentile(r2_diff_boot, 97.5)\\n    \\n    # Cohen's d for R\u00b2 improvement (using correlation conversion)\\n    # Convert R\u00b2 to correlation, then compute d from correlation\\n    r_avg = np.sqrt(np.maximum(r2_avg, 0))  # Avoid negative R\u00b2\\n    r_combined = np.sqrt(np.maximum(r2_combined, 0))\\n    \\n    # Cohen's d from correlation: d = 2r / sqrt(1 - r^2)\\n    # Compute for each fold, then average\\n    d_values = []\\n    for r_a, r_c in zip(r_avg, r_combined):\\n        if r_a < 1 and r_c < 1:\\n            d_a = 2 * r_a / np.sqrt(1 - r_a**2 + 1e-10)\\n            d_c = 2 * r_c / np.sqrt(1 - r_c**2 + 1e-10)\\n            d_values.append(d_c - d_a)  # Difference in d\\n    \\n    cohens_d = np.mean(d_values) if d_values else 0.0\\n    \\n    # Interpretation\\n    abs_d = abs(cohens_d)\\n    if abs_d < 0.2:\\n        interpretation = 'negligible'\\n    elif abs_d < 0.5:\\n        interpretation = 'small'\\n    elif abs_d < 0.8:\\n        interpretation = 'medium'\\n    else:\\n        interpretation = 'large'\\n    \\n    # Percentage variance explained gained\\n    pct_improvement = (mean_diff / np.mean(r2_avg)) * 100 if np.mean(r2_avg) > 0 else 0\\n    \\n    return {\\n        'r2_difference_mean': mean_diff,\\n        'r2_difference_sd': sd_diff,\\n        'r2_difference_ci_95': (ci_lower, ci_upper),\\n        'cohens_d': cohens_d,\\n        'cohens_d_interpretation': interpretation,\\n        'mse_reduction_pct': (1 - np.mean(r2_combined) / np.mean(r2_avg)) * 100,  # Approximate\\n        'practical_significance': 'large' if mean_diff > 0.05 else ('medium' if mean_diff > 0.02 else 'small')\\n    }\\n\\neffect_sizes_weebit = compute_effect_sizes(\\n    {k: {fold: cv_results[k]['test_r2_folds'][i] for i in range(5)} for k in cv_results},\\n    len(y[sources == 'WeeBIT'])\\n)\\n```\\n\\n## Experiment 5: Ablation Study\\n\\n```python\\ndef ablation_study(X, y, n_splits=5):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Ablation study: test each uniformity feature individually.\\n    \\n    Design:\\n    (A) Add-one-in: Start with average features, add one uniformity feature at a time\\n    (B) Remove-one-out: Start with combined features, remove one uniformity feature at a time\\n    \\n    Returns: DataFrame with R\u00b2 for each ablation condition\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    avg_features = ['avg_word_length', 'avg_syllables', 'avg_frequency', 'sentence_length']\\n    uniformity_features = ['cv_word_length', 'cv_syllables', 'cv_frequency']\\n    \\n    results = []\\n    \\n    # Baseline: average only\\n    baseline = cross_val_evaluation(X[avg_features], y, 'Ridge', n_splits)\\n    results.append({\\n        'condition': 'average_only (baseline)',\\n        'features_used': avg_features,\\n        'test_r2_mean': baseline['test_r2_mean'],\\n        'test_r2_sd': baseline['test_r2_sd'],\\n        'r2_above_baseline': 0.0\\n    })\\n    \\n    # Add-one-in ablation\\n    for uf in uniformity_features:\\n        features = avg_features + [uf]\\n        result = cross_val_evaluation(X[features], y, 'Ridge', n_splits)\\n        results.append({\\n            'condition': f'average + {uf}',\\n            'features_used': features,\\n            'test_r2_mean': result['test_r2_mean'],\\n            'test_r2_sd': result['test_r2_sd'],\\n            'r2_above_baseline': result['test_r2_mean'] - baseline['test_r2_mean']\\n        })\\n    \\n    # Full combined\\n    combined_features = avg_features + uniformity_features\\n    combined_result = cross_val_evaluation(X[combined_features], y, 'Ridge', n_splits)\\n    results.append({\\n        'condition': 'combined (all features)',\\n        'features_used': combined_features,\\n        'test_r2_mean': combined_result['test_r2_mean'],\\n        'test_r2_sd': combined_result['test_r2_sd'],\\n        'r2_above_baseline': combined_result['test_r2_mean'] - baseline['test_r2_mean']\\n    })\\n    \\n    # Remove-one-out ablation\\n    for uf in uniformity_features:\\n        features = [f for f in combined_features if f != uf]\\n        result = cross_val_evaluation(X[features], y, 'Ridge', n_splits)\\n        results.append({\\n            'condition': f'combined without {uf}',\\n            'features_used': features,\\n            'test_r2_mean': result['test_r2_mean'],\\n            'test_r2_sd': result['test_r2_sd'],\\n            'r2_drop': combined_result['test_r2_mean'] - result['test_r2_mean']\\n        })\\n    \\n    return pd.DataFrame(results)\\n\\nablation_weebit = ablation_study(X[sources == 'WeeBIT'], y[sources == 'WeeBIT'])\\nablation_cefr = ablation_study(X[sources == 'CEFR-SP'], y[sources == 'CEFR-SP'])\\n\\nprint(\\\"\\\\n\\\" + \\\"=\\\"*60)\\nprint(\\\"ABLATION STUDY RESULTS\\\")\\nprint(\\\"=\\\"*60)\\nprint(ablation_weebit[['condition', 'test_r2_mean', 'r2_above_baseline']].to_string())\\n```\\n\\n## Output Generation: Publication-Ready Tables\\n\\n```python\\ndef generate_method_out(results_dict):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Generate method_out.json    },\\n        'model_performance': {\\n            'weebit': {\\n                'average_only': format_cv_results(cv_results['average_only']),\\n                'uniformity_only':        'weebit': coef_ci_weebit.to_dict('records'),\\n            'cefr_sp': coef_ci_cefr.to_dict('records')\\n        },\\n        'effect_sizes': {\\n            'weebit': effect_sizes_weebit,\\n \\\"\\\"\\\"Format CV results for JSON output (exclude predictions).\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    return {\\n        'test_r2_mean': float(cv_dict['test_r2_mean']),\\n        'test_r2_sd': <hypothesis>
kind: hypothesis
title: Uniformity Improves Sentence Readability
hypothesis: >-
  The readability of a sentence is predicted not only by average linguistic complexity (e.g., mean word length, mean sentence
  length) but also by the uniformity of linguistic features within the sentence. Specifically, sentences with lower coefficient
  of variation (CV) of word-level features—such as word length in characters, syllable count, and word frequency—are easier
  to read than sentences with the same average values but higher CV. Initial experiments on 13,129 sentences from WeeBIT and
  CEFR-SP datasets show that adding uniformity features (CV of word length, syllables, frequency) to traditional average features
  yields statistically significant R² improvements of +0.138 (WeeBIT) and +0.042 (CEFR-SP), both p < 0.0001. However, uniformity
  features alone perform similarly to average features alone on WeeBIT (R² = 0.226 vs 0.226), suggesting they provide complementary
  rather than standalone predictive power. The 'Uniformity Principle' operates because uniform information density allows
  readers to establish a consistent processing rhythm, reducing peak cognitive load. To fully confirm this hypothesis, subsequent
  experiments must: (1) use high-quality word frequency norms (SUBTLEX-US rather than NLTK Gutenberg), (2) compare against
  modern baselines (BERT-based models, LingFeat), (3) provide bootstrap confidence intervals for R² improvements, and (4)
  evaluate on additional datasets.
motivation: >-
  Classic readability formulas (Flesch-Kincaid, etc.) rely exclusively on average values of surface features. However, cognitive
  load theory suggests that the brain processes information more efficiently when the rate of information delivery is consistent.
  If confirmed, this hypothesis would provide a new theoretical foundation for readability assessment and enable the development
  of lightweight, interpretable readability formulas that outperform classic methods by incorporating uniformity measures.
  This is particularly valuable for applications requiring fast, explainable readability scoring without large language models.
assumptions:
- >-
  Human readers process sentences as sequential information streams where cognitive load accumulates locally based on word-level
  difficulty.
- >-
  Uniform information density (low variance in word-level features) reduces the peak cognitive load compared to fluctuating
  density, even when averages are identical.
- >-
  Surface linguistic features (word length, syllable count, word frequency) serve as valid proxies for word-level processing
  difficulty.
- >-
  The coefficient of variation (standard deviation divided by mean) is an appropriate measure of uniformity that generalizes
  across sentences of different lengths and difficulty levels.
investigation_approach: >-
  1. Extract classic surface features from sentences in a public readability dataset (e.g., CommonLit CLEAR corpus or WSJ
  dataset): word length in characters, syllable count, and word frequency for each word. 2. Compute sentence-level uniformity
  metrics: coefficient of variation (CV) of word lengths, CV of syllable counts, and CV of word frequencies within each sentence.
  3. Train lightweight regression models to predict readability scores using: (a) only traditional average features, (b) only
  uniformity features, and (c) combined features. 4. Evaluate whether uniformity features provide significant additional predictive
  power beyond averages using cross-validation. 5. Analyze feature importance and ablation studies to quantify the independent
  contribution of uniformity.
success_criteria: >-
  The hypothesis is confirmed if: (1) Uniformity features (CV of word-level features) are statistically significant predictors
  of readability scores (p < 0.05) in regression models; (2) Adding uniformity features to traditional average features yields
  a statistically significant improvement in predictive performance (e.g., R² increase > 0.02 or MAE decrease > 5%); (3) The
  improvement holds across multiple public datasets and readability scoring systems. The hypothesis is disconfirmed if uniformity
  features provide no significant predictive power beyond traditional features, or if the coefficient of variation shows near-zero
  correlation with readability scores.
related_works:
- >-
  Feng et al. (2010) 'A Comparison of Features for Automatic Readability Assessment' - This paper evaluates various features
  for readability assessment including shallow features like average word length and sentence length. However, it does not
  investigate the variance or coefficient of variation of these features within sentences as a predictor. Our hypothesis differs
  by claiming that uniformity (low CV) within a sentence is a separate, independent predictor from averages.
- >-
  Courtis (2004) 'Corporate report obfuscation: artefact or phenomenon?' - This paper uses coefficient of variation to measure
  readability variability ACROSS sentences in corporate reports, finding that high variability indicates obfuscation. Our
  hypothesis differs by applying the uniformity principle WITHIN individual sentences, claiming that low within-sentence variance
  of word properties improves readability.
- >-
  Eltanbouly et al. (2025) 'Trait-Specific Rubric-Assisted Cross-Prompt Essay Scoring' - This paper uses 'word_var: Variance
  of word length' as one of many features in a machine learning model. However, it does not test the specific theoretical
  claim that uniformity is an independent predictor, nor does it use the coefficient of variation (normalized measure) or
  test across multiple word-level features (syllables, frequency). Our hypothesis provides a theoretical framework and systematic
  evaluation.
- >-
  Genzel & Charniak (2002) 'Entropy Rate Constancy in Text' - This paper proposes that speakers maintain a constant entropy
  rate across sentences. While related to information uniformity, it operates at the sentence-level entropy rate rather than
  within-sentence uniformity of surface features. Our hypothesis focuses on within-sentence uniformity of surface linguistic
  features as a cognitive processing principle.
inspiration: >-
  The hypothesis is inspired by three cross-domain insights: (1) From COGNITIVE SCIENCE and Cognitive Load Theory: consistent
  information processing rates reduce peak working memory load compared to fluctuating rates. (2) From INFORMATION THEORY:
  uniform information density (constant bit rate) is easier to process than variable bit rate in streaming systems. (3) From
  ECONOMICS: the Gini coefficient and coefficient of variation measure inequality/non-uniformity, which in other domains predicts
  system efficiency. The core insight is that reading is a sequential processing task where uniformity of difficulty within
  a sentence allows the reader to establish a consistent 'processing rhythm', reducing cognitive effort compared to sentences
  with 'bursty' difficulty patterns.
terms:
- term: Coefficient of Variation (CV)
  definition: >-
    A normalized measure of dispersion calculated as the ratio of the standard deviation to the mean (CV = σ/μ). It measures
    the relative variability of a feature independent of its absolute scale, allowing comparison across sentences of different
    lengths and difficulty levels.
- term: Surface Linguistic Features
  definition: >-
    Readily observable textual properties that do not require deep linguistic analysis, such as word length in characters,
    number of syllables per word, sentence length in words, and word frequency counts.
- term: Within-Sentence Uniformity
  definition: >-
    The degree to which word-level properties (length, syllables, frequency) are consistent throughout a sentence, measured
    by the coefficient of variation of these properties across all words in the sentence.
- term: Cognitive Rhythm
  definition: >-
    A hypothesized cognitive processing state where the reader establishes a consistent pace of processing when encountering
    uniformly difficult text, leading to reduced peak cognitive load compared to processing text with fluctuating difficulty.
- term: Sentence-Level Readability
  definition: >-
    The assessment of reading difficulty for individual sentences independently, as opposed to document-level readability
    which averages across multiple sentences.
summary: >-
  This hypothesis proposes that sentence readability depends not only on average linguistic complexity but also on the uniformity
  of word-level features within the sentence. Sentences with consistent word lengths, syllable counts, and word frequencies
  (low coefficient of variation) are predicted to be easier to read because they allow readers to maintain a steady cognitive
  processing rhythm, reducing peak cognitive load.
_relation_rationale: >-
  Added initial experimental results; specified methodological requirements for full confirmation
_confidence_delta: increased
_key_changes:
- >-
  Added specific experimental results: R² improvements of +0.138 and +0.042, both p < 0.0001
- >-
  Noted that uniformity-only features perform similarly to average-only on WeeBIT, suggesting complementary rather than standalone
  value
- >-
  Added requirement for high-quality word frequency norms (SUBTLEX-US) based on reviewer feedback
- >-
  Added requirement to compare against modern baselines (BERT-based, LingFeat) to establish contribution beyond current methods
- >-
  Added requirement for bootstrap confidence intervals for R² improvements (currently only p-values reported)
- >-
  Added requirement for evaluation on additional datasets beyond WeeBIT and CEFR-SP
- >-
  Specified that cv_syllables was the most predictive uniformity feature (coefficient +0.150 on WeeBIT)
relation_type: evolution
</hypothesis>

--- Dependency 2 ---
id: art_zKX1_wXmedjn
type: research
title: Word features and readability methods research
summary: |-
  This research artifact provides a comprehensive methodological guide for computing word-level linguistic features (syllable count, word frequency) and understanding the sentence-level readability assessment landscape. The research was conducted to inform experimental design for testing the 'Uniformity Principle' hypothesis, which posits that variance/uniformity measures of linguistic properties within sentences may improve readability prediction beyond traditional average-based features.

  Key findings across 5 research phases:

  1. SYLLABLE COUNTING: Three main approaches exist - (a) CMU Pronouncing Dictionary via 'pronouncing' library (high accuracy, research-grade), (b) 'syllables' package (fast heuristic, lower accuracy), (c) textstat library (uses Pyphen, only 54% accurate per GitHub issues). Recommendation: Use CMUdict as primary with heuristic fallback.

  2. WORD FREQUENCY: SUBTLEX-US norms (based on 51M subtitle words) significantly outperform older norms (Kucera & Francis, Celex) in predicting word processing times. Available as free download from Ghent University. Google Books Ngrams is secondary option.

  3. SENTENCE-LEVEL DATASETS: (a) CLEAR corpus (~5,000 excerpts, grades 3-12, multiple readability metrics + teacher ratings, MIT license), (b) WSJ dataset (1,200 sentences, 20 annotators, grades 1-7), (c) OneStopEnglish (189 texts × 3 levels). CLEAR recommended as primary for hypothesis testing.

  4. FEATURE LANDSCAPE: Feng et al. (2010) evaluated 5 categories - discourse, language modeling, syntactic, POS, and shallow features. Their Table 5 lists 8 shallow features. Critical finding: ALL existing features are means/averages (e.g., 'average syllables per word'). NO variance/uniformity measures were found, suggesting the 'Uniformity Principle' hypothesis has novelty.

  5. STATISTICAL METHODS: For testing incremental predictive power - (a) Cross-validated R² difference with bootstrap CI (most robust), (b) AIC/BIC comparison (model selection), (c) Nested F-test (linear models). Recommendations provided with Python implementation examples.

  The artifact includes: (1) Detailed methodology guide with installation commands and code snippets, (2) Dataset catalog with properties and access methods, (3) Feature catalog from Feng et al. (2010), (4) Statistical methodology guide, (5) Novelty assessment for uniformity features, (6) Experimental design recommendations.

  Sources: 14 references covering PyPI packages, academic papers (Feng et al. 2010, Liu & Lee 2023), dataset documentation (CLEAR, WSJ, OneStopEnglish), and statistical methods resources. All sources accessed and verified via web research tools.

For each bootstrap iteration b:\\n       - Sample n indices with replacement from [0, n-1]\\n       - Fit Model A (average features) and Model B (combined) on bootstrap sample\\n       - Predict on out-of-bag (OOB) samples\\n       - Compute MSE_A and MSE_B on OOB\\n       - Record: mse_diff = MSE_A - MSE_B (positive = B better)\\n    \\n    2.
